Domestic News

Commemorative Week at the Central Government and the National Government 57

Central Party Headquarters On October 6th, at 9:00 AM, the Central Party Headquarters held the 80th weekly memorial service for the late Premier in the main auditorium. Central Committee members Ye Chucang, Chen Lifu, Chen Bulei, Chen Yaoyuan, and other departmental staff and guests, totaling about six to seven hundred people, attended. Chairman Ye Chucang, after commencing the ceremony, gave a report, stating that everyone was likely already aware of the current situation of the Central Party and government, as well as the victories of the anti-rebellion military campaign, so he would not repeat them. However, the central government needed to investigate the current situation of Party affairs and administration in various provinces at any time, and those responsible for the local affairs of each province also needed to report to the central government on the current situation of Party affairs and administration at any time. Jiangsu, with Nanjing as its capital, benefits from the central guidance, making the implementation of Party affairs and administration a focus of both the central government and various local authorities. He would take this opportunity to briefly report on the Party affairs and politics of Jiangsu Province. The Jiangsu Provincial Government had been established for five months. Whether the administration was clean and bright, whether local security was guaranteed, whether the burden on the people had been reduced, and whether the troubles between the Party and the administration had been eliminated could be summarized by saying that none of these had been achieved. He felt that the biggest cause of disputes between the Party and the administration was the protection of subordinates by government offices and the protection of Party members by Party departments. If local officials neglected their duties, higher-level government offices should have noticed it early and punished them according to the law. It felt less than satisfactory when punishment was only meted out after the Party department filed a complaint. If, after the complaint, not only was there no thorough investigation and handling, but there was also a feeling of discomfort, then it would be extremely difficult for both sides to get along, and how could there be any cooperation? He initially thought that by doing things with a clear conscience, some results could be achieved. However, based on the experience of the past few months, he realized that employing people and administering affairs cannot achieve the desired effects solely by relying on conscience. The corruption in handling public security in various counties of Jiangsu Province was truly indescribable. Not only was it not beneficial to the locality, but it also caused much harm to the people. Most counties experienced financial difficulties to pay the police. However, the police station inspector in these places without funds felt that it was even more to his liking, and the behind-the-scenes dealings were imaginable. Therefore, he often felt that it would be better to abolish these corrupt police agencies altogether, but the difficulty was that the regulations did not allow it. Also, for example, the construction land tax in each county had a maximum annual revenue of no more than 4,000 yuan, but the county government had to set up a construction bureau, and the salaries and public expenses of its director, technicians, and other personnel would amount to 3,600 yuan per year. With the remaining 400 yuan, how could construction be discussed? He also felt that it was unnecessary to set up a special bureau and that the county government could appoint technicians to be responsible for handling it, in order to save expenses and free up funds for construction needs, but this was also not allowed by the regulations, so he hoped that attention would be paid to this and that some flexibility would be left in the agency organizational regulations. As for the employment of personnel, it was even more difficult. He used to be not very confident in the ability of the elderly to handle affairs, fearing that they would be old-fashioned, but now he was also not very confident in the ability of young people to handle affairs. There were many excellent young people, but there were also many corrupt ones. Before having a job, they would look everywhere for work, but once they had a job, they would become discouraged and lazy due to some slight difficulties. It was extremely difficult to find truly talented people. With the higher civil service examination not yet completed, it was difficult to find standards for appointing officials. Often, when appointing a county magistrate, they would speak eloquently during the meeting, but after taking office, their performance would be the complete opposite of what they had said. The gathering of talented people was the fundamental condition for a clean administration. Without proper screening, entrusting them with power would inevitably lead to failure, so he also hoped that the policy on the employment of personnel would be determined as soon as possible in order to remedy this. There were many bandits in Jiangsu Province, and they were widespread, even more so than before May, which was truly distressing. The local security forces consisted of only one regiment, which could only cope with the bandits and fulfill the responsibility of defending the territory for the country. They could not talk about suppressing the bandits and relieving the people from their suffering. During this anti-rebellion period, Jiangsu Province was fortunate not to have experienced any major incidents, which was due to the strength of the central garrison forces in the rear, which was enough to deter them. The local forces in Jiangsu Province could not share even one-tenth of the credit. Although the Jiangsu Provincial Government had a plan to establish four security regiments, there was no timetable for its realization, so he still hoped that the central government would send heavy troops to suppress the bandits on a large scale at the end of the anti-rebellion campaign, first clearing the lurking bandits in the vicinity of the capital in order to maintain the order of Nanjing. After the report, the meeting adjourned at 10:30 AM.

National Government On the same morning at 10:00 AM, the National Government held a weekly memorial service for the late Premier. Gu Yingfen, Zhu Peide, Zhang Nanxian, Liu Ruiheng, Zhu Lühe, Chen Yi, Chen Shaokuan, Li Jinlun, Mu Xiangyue, Zhu Jingnong, Zhang Wohua, Chen Yu, Zhou Yawei, Zhang Xiqian, and more than two hundred staff members from the two departments of civil officials and military advisors of the National Government attended. Chairman Gu, after performing the ceremony, heard Secretary Zhu Wenzhong give a political report as follows: In terms of military affairs, the progress in military affairs during this week has been very rapid. Since the central army bravely advanced on the 30th of last month and captured Lanfeng, which the enemy had stubbornly defended for several months, it also captured Qixian and other places on the same day. On the 1st of this month, it captured Zhuxian Town Chenliu, on the 2nd it captured Heshang Bridge Xuchang, on the 3rd it captured Kaifeng, and on the 4th it occupied Zhongmu. It is now besieging Zhengzhou and Luoyang, and it is expected that Zheng and Luo can be captured within a day or two, completely eliminating the remaining forces of the enemy on the Longhai and Pinghan railways. At this time, Feng Yuxiang already knew that his own life was coming to an end, so he created an atmosphere of resignation and going abroad, hoping to save his life. Past facts tell us that Feng Yuxiang's resignation and going abroad have been mentioned several times, but the result was still rebellion and still dreaming of overthrowing the Party and the country. Therefore, what he says now is not only not believed by bystanders, but even his own subordinates are mostly suspicious of each other. Because of mutual suspicion, everyone wants to find a proper way to survive in the future. The ancients said that those who obey Heaven will survive, and those who defy Heaven will perish. Heaven is the natural trend, which means that only by following the natural trend can one survive, and those who defy the natural trend will perish. Feng Yuxiang has repeatedly rebelled, nothing more than wanting to maintain his feudal power, or even go a step further and taste the taste of Hongxian the second and third. This erroneous thinking is completely incompatible with the modern natural trend of democracy. Based on the principle that those who obey Heaven will survive and those who defy Heaven will perish, his demise is inevitable and his survival is impossible. Therefore, his current defeat was already in our budget. This rebellion by Yan and Feng can be said to be the last glimmer of all feudal remnants. After this final suppression by the central government, we believe that there will be no possibility of a resurgence. Before setting off for the front, Chairman Chiang once said that the sooner the counter-revolution breaks out, the sooner the revolution will succeed. This sentence has actually become a reality now, and we should congratulate the Party and the country on its future. The day before yesterday (the 3rd), Chairman Chiang sent a telegram from the front, proposing that the government issue a clear order after the military situation is stabilized, or on January 1, 20, to pardon all political and military criminals, cancel the wanted notices, restore their freedom, and allow them to enjoy the rights that ordinary citizens should have, in order to appease the dissidents, stabilize people's hearts, eliminate the source of chaos, and consolidate the foundation of the country. This proposition of governing people with virtue is completely consistent with the spirit of generosity of the late Premier. Originally, using heavy punishment to govern a chaotic country was only a temporary expedient method. The fundamental plan for the long-term peace and stability of the country should naturally not exceed the two words of benevolence and love mentioned by the late Premier. After this military situation is stabilized, the government will definitely be able to follow Chairman Chiang's proposition and vigorously practice the two words of benevolence and love, in order to implement the great spirit of the late Premier's generosity and all-inclusiveness. In terms of finance, the national likin tax was originally scheduled to be abolished uniformly on October 10th of this year. The Ministry of Finance had already sent personnel to prepare and convened financial personnel from various provinces and economists to hold a meeting to discuss and plan compensation methods, hoping to implement it as scheduled. Unfortunately, after this military incident occurred, the impact affected various provinces, some of which became war zones or had bandit problems. If changes were made now, many malpractices would inevitably occur, which would be harmful and not beneficial to the country and the people. The government, in view of this, decided to postpone the implementation for two months, but it was limited to implementation before January 1, 20, and could not be delayed any further. It can be seen that the government has long been determined to abolish the national likin tax. No matter how difficult it is, it will eventually abolish it completely within this year. In terms of diplomacy, Weihaiwei was officially taken over by our country on the 1st of this month. All takeover procedures have been properly handled. The previous report on the Xiamen British Concession stated that it was recovered on the 17th of last month. On the 1st of this month, Weihaiwei was officially taken over again. Within two weeks, two concessions were recovered. The progress in diplomacy cannot be said to be slow. If we can continue to strive in this spirit, we believe that we will definitely be able to follow the late Premier's will, abolish all unequal treaties in the shortest possible time, and restore our country's inherent position in the international arena. In terms of legal system, recently, the Legislative Yuan has passed the first to fifth parts of the Civil Procedure Law, the National Funeral Law, and the Disaster Relief Reserve Fund Law. Among them, the most noteworthy is the National Funeral Law, which the government promulgated last Friday. The first article states that "citizens of the Republic of China who have made special contributions to the country shall be given a state funeral after their death in accordance with the provisions of this law." According to this provision, all citizens of the Republic of China, as long as they can make special contributions to the country, can enjoy the honor of a state funeral after their death. All the class characteristics in the previous laws have been completely broken. This is the equalization of laws, which is the true spirit of legislation based on the Three Principles of the People, and it is very worthy of our attention.

Supreme Court's Judgment on Gao Ying's Opium Trafficking Case 59

Gao Liao Shi sentenced to four years of imprisonment and a fine of four thousand yuan. Nanjing Dispatch: The Supreme Court, regarding the case of appellants Gao Ying, Gao Liao Shi, Sun Yuan, and others for the crime of selling opium, etc., who appealed against the second instance judgment of the Jiangsu High Court, hereby renders the following judgment according to law:

Main Text: The original judgment is revoked. Gao Liao Shi, with intent to sell, possessed opium and is sentenced to four years of imprisonment, along with a fine of four thousand yuan. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be used to offset the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. If the fine is converted into imprisonment, it shall be calculated at a rate of three yuan for one day, but the imprisonment period shall not exceed one year. The two cans of opium are confiscated and burned. The Gao Ying and Sun Yuan parts are sent back to the Jiangsu High Court for retrial.

Facts: Gao Liao Shi is the wife of Gao Ying, the vice-consul of the U.S. Consulate General in San Francisco. Gao Ying and Gao Liao Shi both reside in San Francisco and are well aware of international practice, where the luggage of consulate personnel and their families can be imported without inspection. Therefore, they took advantage of this opportunity and colluded with Chinese residents in San Francisco whose names are unknown, Shou Nan Ruo Yun, and Hong Kong merchants Wen Yu Xian and Shen Guang, etc., to return to China in January of the 18th year of the Republic of China, and went to Hong Kong to carry 2,299 cans of opium for Wen Yu Xian and Shen Guang, divided into eleven boxes. All boxes were affixed with seals from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government and signatures from the San Francisco Consulate General, and declared as their own luggage. In June of the same year, they took the Tianyang Maru steamer to the United States. On July 5th, the ship arrived in San Francisco. At that time, the U.S. Customs had already detected the situation and immediately detained the luggage carried by Gao Liao Shi, opened the boxes for inspection, and found opium and letters entrusting the delivery of opium, etc. The U.S. court then arrested Gao Liao Shi and others and handed them over to Minister Wu stationed in the United States for extradition back to the country, where the Jiangning District Court Procurator filed a public prosecution.

Reasons: This case should be explained separately. 1. Gao Liao Shi’s part: It has been verified that Gao Liao Shi's suitcases carried from China to the United States contained 2,299 cans of opium. The boxes were affixed with seals from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government and signatures from the Chinese Consulate General in San Francisco. U.S. Customs inspectors Harris and Manager Smith searched out the aforementioned opium in her boxes and issued certificates attached to the file. Although Gao Liao Shi argued, "The boxes containing opium were entrusted by Mr. and Mrs. Chen, and I did not know what was hidden inside. They only said that someone would come to pick them up when they arrived in San Francisco," Gao Liao Shi has consistently refused to disclose Mr. Chen's address, making it doubtful whether it is true. Moreover, four letters were found in Gao Liao Shi's own box, all of which were photographed and submitted to the case. One was a letter from Wen Yu Xian and Shen Guang to Sun Yuan, which stated, "Now I hand over a foreign box to the person coming." The second was a letter from Shen Guang to Ruo Yun, which stated, "Now I hand over nine foreign boxes to Mr. Gao." The third was a letter from Yu Xian and Shen Guang to Shou Nan, which stated, "Now I hand over two foreign boxes to the person coming." The fourth was a letter from Wen Yu Xian to Sun Yuan, which stated, "Brother, please open the foreign boxes yourself and check the numbers before handing them over." These letters and the keys to the boxes storing opium were found in Gao Liao Shi's box. Harris and Smith have indeed provided separate proofs, and Gao Liao Shi also admits that there is no difference. If Gao Liao Shi did not know what was stored in the box, why were the letters sent by Wen Yu Xian, etc., stored in her own box? Why would Wen Yu Xian and Shen Guang entrust the opium, which is worth a huge amount, to Gao Liao Shi? How could Gao Liao Shi not investigate the matter and immediately regard the box as her own luggage and fill it in on the luggage list? In reference to Gao Ying's telegram to Minister Wu stating, "The boxes contain a small amount of drugs, which my wife was persuaded to bring," it is even more evident that Gao Liao Shi knew beforehand that she was carrying opium, and the matter is very obvious. Furthermore, the letter from Wen Yu Xian and Shen Guang to Shou Nan stated, "150 branches of K-character Korean ginseng, each branch costing 85 yuan, and each branch paying 10 yuan for labor. 280 branches of Chang-character Korean ginseng, each branch costing 70 yuan, and each branch paying 5 yuan for labor." It also stated, "Please telegraph back for peace and price when receiving the goods." As evidenced by the seized opium cans, there are indeed two types, K-character and Chang-character, which shows that the Korean ginseng mentioned in the letter is a euphemism for opium. The so-called labor and price refer to the original transportation fee and selling price. What is stated in the letter is a comprehensive plan prepared for sale. Reviewing Gao Liao Shi’s behavior, although it has not reached the level of selling, there is no room for argument about her intent to sell and possession of this opium. Before Gao Liao Shi sold it, she carried the opium to the United States for Wen Yu Xian, etc., which is a direct and important act of helping with possession and cannot be convicted of selling. However, the original judgment considered it as attempted assistance in selling, citing Article 6 and Article 12 of the Anti-Smoking Law and Article 44, Paragraph 1 and Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law, which is obviously a misunderstanding and should be corrected by this court according to law. 2. Gao Ying’s part: It has been verified that the opium suitcases carried by Gao Liao Shi were affixed with seals from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and signatures from the San Francisco Consulate General, which the San Francisco Consulate General photographed and submitted to the case. These seals and signatures are necessary items for secretly hiding opium and avoiding inspection. Gao Ying is the vice-consul of the Consulate General, and these seals and signatures happen to be affixed to Gao Liao Shi’s suitcases. When Gao Liao Shi’s luggage was detained by U.S. Customs, Gao Ying repeatedly telegraphed Minister Wu, stating, "For the sake of preserving national dignity, it is absolutely imperative not to open and inspect." He also stated, "I implore your honorable consulate to negotiate with the Ministry of Finance and immediately telegraph the Customs to stop opening and inspecting, otherwise the consequences will be unimaginable." He and Sun Yuan went to the Customs to negotiate for exemption from inspection and release. From all these aspects, Gao Ying’s suspicion of being an accomplice is indeed significant. However, the signature of the consulate does not have a seal, and it is doubtful whether it belongs to the San Francisco Consulate and was issued by Gao Ying. Moreover, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs seal is not pre-issued to each consulate for backup, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has replied that this is on record. Even if the seal used by Gao Liao Shi was indeed obtained from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Gao Ying is far away in the United States, and it cannot be said that he is related to Gao Ying. As for Gao Ying’s initial contact with Sun Yuan at the Customs and his subsequent telegram requesting Minister Wu to negotiate for exemption from inspection and release, his repeated attempts to cover up whether he was trying to avoid his own crime or whether he acted to protect Gao Liao Shi are worthy of investigation. The original trial did not conduct a thorough investigation and hastily convicted him, which is somewhat rash. Furthermore, Chen Yi sent repeated letters to Gao Ying, stating that there were four Chinese laborers going to the United States and asking him to help them land, promising him a generous reward. When the Chinese laborers Mei Guang, Mei Geng, Wu Zhuo, and Lu Huan arrived in the United States, it was discovered that their passports had been altered and that they had misused the name of the revoked Mexican consulate, so the Chinese laborers were sent back. Not only did Chen Yi clearly state this, but Gao Ying also admitted that there was no difference. Reviewing Chen Yi’s letter to Gao Ying, it stated, "Now there are three or four people who want to go to the United States. Can I take a diplomatic passport on behalf of my brother? Can you help them land? If so, I will reward 3,000 yuan per person, and I will take one-fourth." Another letter replying to Gao Ying stated, "Before receiving the telegram, they had already boarded, so they had to go back to Shanghai. The letter received said that the Mexican name cannot be used. Fortunately, only one person used it. I don’t know what the result will be. The money could have been 3,000, but it was changed to 2,400, and I have asked them to add 2,600." Observing these two letters, it is clear that Chen Yi sent Chinese laborers to the United States, requesting Gao Ying to help them land. Gao Ying not only did not refuse but also said that the Mexican name could not be used, instructing them on how to go to the United States. When the Chinese laborers arrived in the United States, Gao Ying falsely claimed that two of them were his personal servants and asked the Consul General to find ways to help them. Gao Ying also clearly admitted this, and Sun Yuan vividly stated how he profited from it. It is clear that Gao Ying and Chen Yi agreed on a reward to help Chinese laborers land, and the evidence is conclusive, leaving no room for argument. The original trial considered that helping Chinese laborers land was an act within the scope of consular duties, and Gao Ying, as the vice-consul, agreed on a reward for his duties, which should constitute the crime of agreeing to a bribe under Article 128, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, which is not without merit. However, Article 1, Item 1 of the Consular Officer Duty Regulations states that resident consuls general, consuls, and vice-consuls in the jurisdiction of the country where they are stationed have the duties of developing the country's commerce and comforting overseas merchants.

Page 8

Whether Gao Ying’s assistance in landing the Chinese laborers Mei Guang, Mei Geng, Wu Zhuo, Lu Huan, etc., is within the scope of his duties is questionable. Although Article 8 and Article 9 of the same regulation state that consular duties are not limited to commercial matters, and the official letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to the first instance stated that the consular duty is to protect overseas Chinese, so although there are no explicit regulations on arrival and assistance, such matters are also necessary if there is an actual need. However, whether Gao Ying’s assistance in landing Mei Guang, Mei Geng, Wu Zhuo, Lu Huan, etc., falls within the scope of actual necessity, in addition to the original letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, whether there are other orders or events in the Ministry that can confirm that assisting Chinese laborers in landing is a type of consular duty, is worth investigating. The original trial did not conduct a detailed investigation and used only the official letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs as the sole basis for conviction without explaining how Gao Ying’s assistance in landing Chinese laborers fit the situation indicated in the original letter, and hastily made a judgment, which is inappropriate. The intention to appeal regarding that part is not entirely without reason. 3. Sun Yuan’s part: It has been verified that the letter from Wen Yu Xian and Shen Guang to Sun Yuan contained in Gao Liao Shi's box stated, "Now I hand over foreign boxes to the person coming, a total of nine boxes from number one to number nine, for Ruo Yun to receive. Also, two foreign boxes for Shou Nan to receive. But when you arrive, please first send the foreign boxes to Brother Ruo Yun and Brother Shou Nan according to the letter, so that the foreign boxes can be handed over. Please telegraph back for peace." In addition, Wen Yu Xian sent another letter stating, "Brother, please open the foreign boxes yourself and check boxes number two and number eleven and hand them over to Brother Shou Nan. Please give the rest to Brother Fu." The numbers are inside the box and will be seen as soon as it is opened. It can be generally seen that Sun Yuan and Wen Yu Jia have a close relationship. However, according to Sun Yuan's defense, "I do not know Yu Xian, Shen Guang, Shou Nan, or Ruo Yun, and I know nothing about Gao Liao Shi carrying opium." If this is true, how dare Wen Yu Xian and Shen Guang entrust him to deliver the opium, which is worth a huge amount? Moreover, since Wen Yu Xian, Shen Guang, etc., entrusted Gao Liao Shi to carry the opium, if they had not contacted Sun Yuan beforehand, Gao Liao Shi could have directly handed it over to Shou Nan and Ruo Yun. It is clear that the various claims presented by Sun Yuan are unreasonable. It has been verified that when Gao Liao Shi's ship arrived in San Francisco, Sun Yuan personally greeted her at the pier. When Gao Liao Shi's luggage was detained, Sun Yuan introduced Gao Ying to negotiate with Customs, which Sun Yuan himself clearly admitted. By comparing and verifying, Sun Yuan’s suspicion of committing a crime is indeed not insignificant. The original trial used this to determine the facts, which is not without merit. However, a review of the litigation records shows that Sun Yuan consistently denied conspiring with Gao Liao Shi to commit a crime, and an examination of the letters sent by Wen Yu Xian, etc., also does not provide evidence of prior conspiracy. Whether Sun Yuan conspired with Gao Liao Shi beforehand to carry opium to the United States this time, and whether his presence at the San Francisco pier and introduction of Gao Ying to negotiate with Customs can be regarded as acts of sharing responsibility for the crime should all be thoroughly investigated. The original trial did not thoroughly investigate the circumstances before and after and hastily made a judgment, which seems to be insufficient to fulfill the ability to investigate. It should all be sent back for retrial to form a credible conviction. Based on the above arguments, it should be the same as Article 409 of the Criminal Procedure Law, Article 410, Paragraph 1, Item 1, Article 2 and Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law, Article 9 and Article 44, Paragraph 1, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law, the latter half of Article 64, Article 55, Paragraph 3 and Paragraph 4, Article 14 of the Anti-Smoking Law, and Article 413 of the Criminal Procedure Law. The judgment is as stated in the main text.

Bandit Atmosphere on the Border of Jiangsu and Shandong 60

Rizhao County suffers devastation. Qingdao Correspondence: Rizhao County is located on the border of Shandong and Jiangsu. Residents along the eastern coast live by fishing and salt production. The northwest is mountainous, and residents rely on firewood and grazing for a living. The land is barren, the people are poor, and there has never been banditry. In recent times, although bandits are everywhere, the residents of the county are still able to live and work in peace because of its coastal location. Even if bandit alerts occur, they are only caused by local unscrupulous ruffians. Unexpectedly, since the beginning of last month, about four or five hundred bandits suddenly arrived from Yizhou and Mengyin, entrenched in the southwest of Jufeng Township in the county, killing, setting fires, and devastating dozens of villages. The Qingdao native association of the county, aware that the banditry in the county is becoming increasingly urgent, specially convened a meeting of natives today (3rd) to discuss ways to quell the banditry. It was decided to elect representatives to go to Qingdao and Jinan to request the military authorities to send troops to suppress the bandits. It is also heard that the navy has agreed to send marines to intercept nearby as soon as the provincial troops arrive, in order to eradicate them in one fell swoop. (October 3rd)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 61

Water police arrest five bandits. Fan Guozhong, the first team leader of the first district of the Songjiang Water Police Provincial Public Security Team, said that the junction of Songyi, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang is riddled with bandits. In recent months, he arrested three bandits, including Zhang Xiaodi, i.e., Xiao Lin, and seized four long and short guns. Later, the local area was slightly quieter. Yesterday, in Shanghai, Fangjia arrested five notorious thieves, including Yu Guixiang, Wan Ruiyun, and Chen Caiqin, the main leaders of local thievery who hid their loot. They have already confessed to more than ten cases of kidnapping and theft, such as Jiaodiao Bay. The crimes are obvious and have been sent to the Songjiang County Government for legal processing.

County Magistrate Arrests Corrupt District Chief: Chen Ziwen, the chief of the ninth district, was previously accused of corruption in grain distribution. The county government reported to the provincial office and ordered his immediate dismissal and retention for investigation. County Magistrate Jin, in addition to appointing Zhu Qianxian, a staff member of this government, to take temporary custody, also sent staff member Liu Meichu to the district to immediately detain him. However, when they arrived at the district, they only saw assistant clerks and other personnel. After inquiring, they learned that he had left the office on the 29th of last month and his whereabouts were unknown. After Liu returned to Songjiang to report, County Magistrate Jin, considering that the district chief's family lived in Caojing, sent political police chief Dong Futang to investigate and arrest him with a warrant.

Jiading 62

Citizens Request Exemption from Provincial Road Diversion: The original route of the Zhenhu Provincial Road ran westward from the west gate of Jiading through Beishi, Waigang Town, then northward through Gelong Town, and into Taicang. Recently, the Construction Department suddenly ordered the route to be diverted south of Muduhang, directly impacting the center of Waigang Town and requiring the demolition of more than one hundred public and private houses in the town. The local citizens, upon learning of this, were alarmed and petitioned the county government and the Construction Bureau to exempt the change. It is now heard that the county bureau and the Construction Bureau have telegraphed the situation to the Construction Department, but it is not known whether they will be granted permission.

Refugees Escorted Out of the County: On the 3rd, more than two hundred refugees arrived in Nanxiang, a town in the county. The town's Public Security Bureau dispatched police to maintain order, and Town Mayor Fei Meishan distributed rations and ordered them to leave the county. Unexpectedly, the refugees were unwilling and fled towards Sijing. The Public Security Bureau then dispatched police to chase them down and, together with the Sijing Security Regiment, escorted them to Nanxiang Railway Station and forced them onto the train to Kunshan. It is heard that the refugees are from Huangmei County, Hubei, and had harassed Yinxian County, Zhejiang, and were escorted to Shanghai, from where the Shanghai Public Security Bureau escorted them to Jiading.

Fengxian 63

Market Property Tax Receipts Issued by the Bureau: The market property tax in the towns and streets of this county is used for local public patrol and police expenses. Therefore, the tax receipts issued have always been issued by the local sub-bureaus. Later, although the collection of taxes was changed to the Financial Bureau, the tax receipt format was still printed and issued in the old style, resulting in inconsistent styles and separate registration. Now, Wang Zhuofu of the Financial Bureau, in order to eliminate fraud and clarify the plan, has specially revised the procedures for collection and also issued a general order that from this month onwards, all tax receipts will be made and issued by the bureau and will have the bureau's seal stamped on the seams to show seriousness.

Suzhou 64

Robbery in Shishe Village: The family of Liu Rusheng, a farmer in Shishe Village, Shitang Town, Hengjing, was suddenly visited by eight or nine bandits last night. Two box cannons and iron rulers were used to first bind and injure the 70-year-old grandmother and Liu's mother. More than 300 yuan and clothing were robbed. When leaving, they also kidnapped the victim across the Lian Bridge in Shitang and threw him down only when they reached Huangyong.

Gong Guoliang Dismissed: Gong Guoliang, the district chief of the Third District of the Water Public Security, was dismissed yesterday (6th) by an order from the Civil Affairs Department. The vacancy was filled by Shen Weikuai (Gao Chen (from Wuxian)). After receiving the order, Gong immediately ordered the department to sort out the accumulated cases and all documents in preparation for the handover. It is heard that Shen will take over on the Double Tenth Festival after being appointed.

Acting Team Leaders Ordered Back: Huai Zongbang, the team leader of the Fourteenth Team of the Water Public Security stationed in Wujiang, and Du Jingwu, the team leader of the First Squad, died one after another. The district chief appointed guerrilla captain Fang Yue to act as the team leader of the Fourteenth Team, and the pioneer officer of the district headquarters, Shi Zhen, to act as the team leader of the First Squad. Yesterday, after District Chief Gong was dismissed, he immediately ordered Captain Fang and Pioneer Officer Shi to be transferred to Suzhou. The vacant positions were assigned to Cheng Yougong, the Fourteenth Team clerk, and the Second Squad member.

Zhang Minggao Taken Back to Zhejiang for Trial: Zhang Minggao, the notorious bandit who captured Sian, was arrested in Shanghai's French Concession at No. 12 Youqing Lane by Yang Baokang and Yu Zibin, detectives from the Third District of the Water Public Security, and taken to Suzhou. The previous night, District Chief Gong questioned him and telegraphed the Zhejiang Jiahu Bandit Suppression Command, which sent personnel to Suzhou to escort him back to be dealt with. Yesterday (6th), the Jiahu Bandit Suppression Command sent Lieutenant Lian Feng to Suzhou, holding a document to the Third District Office to take Zhang and return him for trial.

Wuxi 65

Xiliang Ferries Robbed at Jiuligou: In recent years, the ferry business between Wuxi and Liyang has been very prosperous. Five companies operate daily. On the morning of the previous day, four ships departed from Liyang to Wuxi at the same time. One was Xin Jiangcheng of the Changli Line Yangxian Company, one was Guoshan, which passed through Liyang from Zhangzhu to Wuxi, and the other two were Yonggu and Zhonghua, of the Xili Line Yonggu Zhonghua Company. Xin Jiangcheng and Guoshan departed half an hour earlier than Yonggu and Zhonghua. They passed Pinquankou, a key route from Wuxi, Changzhou, and Yixing through Liyang. After passing this, they exited Jiuligou, a key point for Liyang along Taihu Lake. The area is extremely remote, with very few residents and reeds growing on both sides. While the two ships were sailing, gunshots were suddenly heard, and bullets flew past. The whole ship was terrified. At that time, five or six dozen bandits with long guns on the shore shouted for the ships to stop. The ships had no choice but to stop. Many bandits boarded the ships and robbed passengers on both ships, and no one was spared. It is estimated that a total of five or six thousand yuan was lost, and ten people with more ornate clothes were kidnapped. At this time, the Yonggu and Zhonghua, which were sailing behind, had already sailed more than half a mile away. The bandits immediately lowered the tugboat of the Xin Jiangcheng and chased directly, frequently firing shots to show off their power. The Yonggu and other two ships sped up and fled for their lives, but the bandits chasing on the shore were also forced to a small bay and could not cross it, so they were able to escape. After arriving in Xushe, they reported to the local police and security regiment to investigate and strictly investigate the whereabouts of the stolen goods and kidnappings. The Xin Jiangcheng small ferry that was driven away by the bandits has not yet returned.

Wuxi Silk Factories Unanimously Decide to Close Down: The Wuxi Silk Factory Trade Association convened a temporary members' meeting the other day to discuss important issues such as opposing public quantity inspections. Twenty-seven members from thirty-three factories attended, and Qian Fenghao was publicly elected as chairman. The conference situation is as follows: (1) The chairman reported that the Shanghai-Wuxi counterparts had previously decided to stop work in all factories when it was absolutely necessary due to opposition to public quantity inspections. Now the silk market is sluggish, and factory losses are even greater, and they are unable to maintain it. Most factories in Shanghai have closed down, and some workers have voluntarily reduced wages and canceled bonuses in order to reduce costs. What should the factories in Wuxi do? After discussion, it was decided that the issue of public quantity inspections has not been resolved, and silk sales are becoming increasingly stagnant. Each factory can no longer maintain it. The factories in this city decided to temporarily close down from today onwards in accordance with Shanghai's methods. Those involved in silk unwinding may close down together after the silk unwinding is finished. (2) Shanghai Yongyu Silk Factory sent a letter reporting that the Shanghai silk industry had decided to request the government to issue funds to maintain it because of excessive losses and inability to maintain it. The factories in Wuxi have the same joys and sorrows. How should they handle it? It was decided to unite with the factories in Shanghai and request the government to allocate funds for relief.

Cold Waterfront Port Robbed in Broad Daylight: A local mountain goods store in this city specially sent a shop assistant to hire a boat to the countryside to collect debts for the approaching old Mid-Autumn Festival. Yesterday (6th), they returned to the city. At 11:00 a.m., the boat arrived at the Lengdugang area of the Second District (Jingyun City). Unexpectedly, five bandits dressed in tattered uniforms, resembling scattered soldiers, suddenly shouted loudly and forced them to stop. Seeing that the situation was not good, the debt collection boat immediately set sail. The bandits then saw a fishing boat parked nearby and immediately jumped on board, ordering the boatman to row and chase after them. They were caught up. The bandits then swarmed aboard and robbed them at will, and took out weapons, threatening them to remain silent. After half an hour, they left the boat after a full robbery. Upon inspection, it was found that 40 yuan in debts had been robbed. At the same time, a manure boat was also passing by and was also boarded and robbed by the bandits, who only robbed them of one silver yuan.

Pinghu 66

Using Counterfeit Bills and Committing Opium Crimes: Xiao Lu San, who lives in Chujiawan, west of the county, asked the mother of a Chen woman, a concubine of the Shuyuan Lane, to use many counterfeit banknotes from a certain bank in a cigarette paper shop. Two of them had already been used. When using the third one, he was caught by the shop and sent to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. He confessed that Xiao Luo San had asked him to use them. The Public Security Bureau immediately dispatched police to arrest Luo San and also arrested an opium addict, Chen Yisheng (i.e., Chen the Monk), and immediately sent them to the county. Yesterday (4th) afternoon, the court opened the trial. The old woman confessed that Luo San asked her to use the bills on his behalf and that she did not know they were counterfeit, and asked for leniency. Xiao Luo San confessed that the three counterfeit bills were all obtained at a certain large gambling house in Shanghai. The official then asked about the opium case, and Luo San confessed without hesitation. He then interrogated Chen the Monk, who confessed that he had been smoking for 20 years. As a result, the old woman and Luo San were each fined 300 yuan, and those who could not pay were sentenced to 300 days of detention. In the opium case, Xiao Luo San was sentenced to two months of imprisonment, and Chen the Monk was sentenced to one month.

Telephone Price Increase Must Be Implemented: The Zhenjiang Telephone Bureau previously notified all users that it would increase the monthly fee by one yuan. The users believed that it should not be increased repeatedly and publicly requested the Chamber of Commerce to repeatedly telegraph the Ministry of Communications to dispute the matter. The Ministry acknowledged that it would be implemented from January next year. Now the Ministry believes that this case involves government orders and is not easy to change. Yesterday, it specially telegraphed the Zhenjiang Telephone Bureau to notify all users that they would still be charged from September and ordered the Chamber of Commerce to persuade all users to comply with the order.

Liuhe County Representatives Come to the Province to Request Troops: In recent days, banditry has been rampant in the various townships of Liuhe County. Kidnapping, extortion, arson, killing, and burning are all being carried out. Merchants and citizens are unable to sleep peacefully, and even the ripe crops in the various townships do not dare to harvest. The people are in extreme panic. Representatives were publicly elected to come to the province to meet with Chairman Ye at the provincial government to personally present all the circumstances and request that troops be sent to the county to suppress the bandits. Chairman Ye agreed to send troops for suppression in the shortest possible time. The representatives were satisfied and returned to Liuhe today.

Dingfengxiang Silk Factory Has a Dispute: Since the new cocoons came on the market, the Dingfengxiang Silk Factory in Zhenjiang has only worked for 57 days, with the rest of the time spent in shortage and stagnation. The female workers, because the factory has not started work for a long time, have had several labor strikes. After mediation, it was agreed that the car would be restarted at the end of the month. Now, due to the relationship between the old festivals, the female workers have asked the factory to issue the original wages and each borrow another three yuan. In order to maintain the lives of the workers, the factory agreed to the request. However, the female workers in the cocoon copying room were not given the same treatment. Therefore, the female workers in that room gathered at the entrance of the factory this morning (5th) to ask the factory owner to refuse, which led to mutual quarrels and a big dispute. It is still unknown how it will be resolved.

Gaoyou 70

District Chief Extortion Case: Second Trial Record: The previous case of Wu Kai, the district chief of the 8th district of this county, being sued in the county government by villager Shen Dejiu and others for intimidation and extortion, was re-examined yesterday (the 3rd) at 5:00 PM. Fan, the police inspector, and Zhang Sixin were summoned to court for further questioning of the defendant, Wu Kai, and the witnesses. Neither the defendant, Wu Kai, nor the witnesses were present. According to Zhang Sixin's testimony, Wu Kai used an official letter on the 15th to borrow police officers from my station. I lent him two officers at the time. At 9:00 AM on the 16th, he sent villager Shen Dejiu to my station. At that time, I was outside having tea and was called back by my orderly. Wu Kai then said to me, "Detain villager Shen Dejiu here." That afternoon, I went to the city to attend a police affairs meeting. As for the court hearing in the countryside and the release of Shen Dejiu and others, I know nothing about it. According to the testimony of other individuals, their statements were the same as before. After the questioning was completed, an order was issued to compel the defendant, Wu Kai, to appear in court for questioning on bail.

Qingjiang 71

Prisoners Compete for Increased Rations: There are a total of 140 to 150 prisoners detained in the Huaiyin County Prison and the detention center, including over 80 criminals and over 60 individuals detained for military purposes or held by the High Court branch. The prison official in charge and head of the detention center, Zhu Bao, previously, due to soaring rice prices, found that the funds allocated for prisoner rations were insufficient to cover expenses. Therefore, he added kidney beans to the prisoner's meals to reduce costs. However, recently, with the sharp drop in rice prices, the prisoners in the prison or the detention center were still being served meals with kidney beans. As a result, the prisoners rioted in the prison. For a time, outsiders were unaware of the situation. Everyone was concerned. After Acting County Magistrate Xiong Wenmin, judge Shen Shouling, and Public Security Bureau Chief Zhao Zhenhua arrived at the prison to quell the unrest, two representatives were selected from among the prisoners, Pan Bingqing and Shi Weigao, to speak to Acting County Magistrate Xiong and others. They stated that the daily ration for each prisoner was insufficient based on the amount of rice stipulated by the High Court (20 taels of rice), and kidney beans were being added, and requested that the deducted rice be returned in full to prevent the prisoners from starving. Finally, the matter was resolved when Director Zhu agreed to stop adding kidney beans to the prisoner's meals starting on the 5th, and the situation subsided.

Letter Received

Letter from Wang Jiwu, Magistrate of Jingjiang County 73

I recently read the Jingjiang correspondence in your newspaper issue of September 29th, which contained an item about a conflict between our county magistrate and Judge Yin, and the Jiangyin correspondence in the October 4th issue, which mentioned County Magistrate Li retaining Judge Yang. Both of these are inconsistent with the facts. I now provide a summary of the events and inaccuracies below. On September 25th, our government, based on a report, apprehended a man named Xia Yilong (not Liu Yaofang) for a smoking offense. Judge Yin sentenced him to four months of imprisonment and a fine of thirty yuan. The next day, the director and deputy director of the Funds and Property Office came to the government office, requesting bail for Xia, stating that he was seriously ill. Judge Yin ordered him to pay a bail of 300 yuan. Our county magistrate believed that since Xia's original sentence was only a fine of thirty yuan, and he was now granted bail due to illness, demanding a bail ten times the amount of the fine would not only be beyond the offender's means but also provide ammunition for those who like to stir up trouble. Unexpectedly, Judge Yin had other intentions and insisted on his own opinion, speaking with a stern tone. Our county magistrate, being responsible for his duties, could not help but reprimand him slightly. Judge Yin, in a fit of anger, left for Suzhou on his own without obtaining permission from the High Court or the consent of our county magistrate. When our county magistrate went to the court, Chief Judge Lin instructed him in person that Judge Yin's actions were inappropriate and had already been reprimanded, and Yang Junying had been appointed to replace him. He also instructed our county magistrate to supervise him strictly in the future. Our county magistrate, believing that Judge Yin had already been transferred, generously let bygones be bygones and did not report his past work or the fact that he had been repeatedly accused in detail. This is the situation regarding the replacement of our county judge. As for what your newspaper reported on the 4th of this month, that disputes repeatedly arose over the distribution of fines, and that over five hundred citizens of the county, including Jiang Huanmin, accused our county magistrate of embezzling over 50,000 yuan in public funds, all public funds in Jingyi are managed by specialized agencies. Our county magistrate has never handled a single penny other than for supervision. If the reference is to fines from smoking cases, since our county magistrate took office, the total has been no more than 10,000 yuan. After purchasing stamps in accordance with regulations, the remainder has been used as rewards for informants and those who assisted in the capture of offenders, such as the Public Security Bureau, the legal department, and the police, in accordance with regulations. Monthly reports are submitted to the court and the Civil Affairs Department and published in the county government gazette. There have never been any disputes, let alone embezzlement. A thorough search has revealed that there is no such person as Jiang Huanmin in Jingyi. This must be the work of someone harboring private grudges. Once we receive instructions from the court, we will submit a request to investigate the matter strictly in accordance with the law. Fearing that false information will be spread and confuse listeners, I am writing this letter to request a prompt correction. Sincerely, Wang Jiwu, Magistrate of Jingjiang County, October 5th.

Important Education News

The Past and Present of the Rural Normal School System 74

However, those following the instructions of the University Council in August of the 17th year are temporarily allowed to continue as before. The Ministry of Education, based on a report from the Guangdong Provincial Department of Education, stated that the student admission qualifications and length of study specified in the resolution plan of the Second National Education Conference differ from the normal school system promulgated by the former University Council. It requested separate verification and instructions to be followed. The report stated briefly that the former University Council promulgated the normal school system and ordered its affiliated institutions to comply, limiting the establishment of one rural normal school in each area before August of the 18th year, which is on file. In May of this year, the Ministry ordered that rural normal classes should be operated in accordance with the resolutions of the Second National Education Conference, namely (rural normal schools enroll three types of students: (1) graduates of junior high school receive three years of training, (2) those with a high school education and an age of 15 or older receive six years of training, (3) those who are currently rural elementary school teachers and have an equivalent level of education to junior high school receive three years of training. The Ministry also ordered that two-year and three-year rural normal classes run by provincial normal schools should be operated with reference to the plan for establishing various teacher training institutions passed by this National Education Conference. It is noted that the methods for enrolling students and the length of study listed in the plan for establishing various teacher training institutions passed by the Second National Education Conference differ from the normal school system promulgated by the former University Council. However, the resolution plan of the Second National Education Conference has not yet been formally promulgated, and the normal school system established by the former University Council has not been explicitly abolished. Currently, rural normal schools in various regions that are operating in accordance with the previous system should not be ordered to change to the methods specified in the plan. All students in each school who have completed their studies and passed the examination should be allowed to graduate as before. As for students enrolled in the 18th academic year, who have completed one academic year, how should their admission qualifications and length of study be specified? It is appropriate to submit a request for verification and compliance. Furthermore, the length of study for rural normal schools specified in the resolution plan of the Second National Education Conference is six years for those entering after graduating from elementary school and three years for those entering after graduating from junior high school, which is the same as the length of study for the senior high school normal科 of normal schools. Considering the situation, students taking the examination are more likely to enter normal schools and the senior high school normal科 rather than rural normal schools. If the methods specified in the plan are followed, it is feared that it will not be possible to promote them without hindrance. Should the enrollment of students and the length of study for rural normal schools in the 19th academic year still follow the previous system, or should they be changed to operate in accordance with the plan? It is requested that a unified decision be made. The Ministry of Education instructed that the report be acknowledged. Students in rural normal classes enrolled by middle schools and normal schools in the province, whose admission qualifications and length of study are in accordance with Instruction No. 539 of the former University Council in August of the 17th year, are temporarily allowed to continue to operate as before until the new system is promulgated.

The Beijing Civil Training Association Has Issued Permits in Succession (Central News Agency) Since the Central Government promulgated the new organizational procedures for popular organizations in the Republic of China, the Beijing Municipal Public Training Committee has complied by separately instructing various popular organizations in Beijing, such as industry and commerce, to reorganize accordingly. Regarding student associations in various schools, they have recently been submitting requests to the Civil Training Association for permits to reorganize and establish student self-government associations. The Northeast Three Provinces Museum Officially Opens 76

Eleven New Committee Members Appointed

Plans for Careful Management and Expansion

Shenyang Correspondence: The Northeast Three Provinces Museum is located at the former site of the Shenyang Imperial Palace. Initially, the provincial authorities appointed Chou Yuting as the director to prepare for everything. When 文选主 served as the head of Liaoning Province, he appointed seven members of the preparatory committee, with Jin Liang as the chairman, to assist in the preparations. Over the past two or three years, the artifacts stored in the Forbidden City have been displayed and opened to the public, achieving considerable success. Recently, Provincial Chairman 　Shy Shi-yi believed that the museum was of great importance to the old culture of the three northeastern provinces and should be vigorously expanded to facilitate development. Furthermore, since the museum's preparatory period had passed, it should be officially opened. Therefore, the provincial government separately stipulated the museum's regulations, implemented a committee system, and appointed eleven new committee members. The committee consists of one chairman and two standing committee members, who are responsible for the museum's affairs. As for the museum's facilities, in addition to the old artifacts, hundreds of types of old palace-collected woodblock-printed books and old Manchu archives have been completely organized, displayed, and opened for reading. Therefore, the museum's affairs are divided into two departments: artifacts and books. Recently, the provincial government has appointed the new committee members. The chairman is still Jin Liang. The committee members include Wu Jiaxiang, the director of the Department of Education; Mu Yuanzhi, the provincial government counselor; Chou Yuting, the former director of the museum; Zhao Jingqi, the former director of the Department of Administration; Dai Yuhuang, the former director of the Weights and Measures Bureau; Ji Zhenduo, the current president of the Education Association; Wang Huayi; Li Xianggeng, the secretary of the chief executive's office; Bian Hongru, the director of the provincial library; and Jin Kuijun, a famous scholar in Shenyang. Jin Kuijun has been appointed as the standing committee member of the Artifacts Department, and Bian Hongru has been appointed as the standing committee member of the Books Department. Yesterday, the committee members held their first meeting to discuss and formulate plans for organizing and expanding the museum. Each committee member is responsible for planning and implementing the plans separately.

Anhui Education Funds to be Issued Immediately: 180,000 Yuan 78

The Financial Commissioner's Office Releases 80,000 Yuan and Borrows 100,000 Yuan

The Anhui Financial Commissioner's Office owes a total of 240,000 yuan in allocated education funds. The various provincial schools in Anhui have been in arrears for two months. The principals of the provincial schools went to Wuhu one after another to demand the funds from the Financial Commissioner's Office. A total of fifteen principals have submitted requests, accounting for three-quarters of the provincial schools. After repeated negotiations on the 29th and 30th, the Financial Commissioner's Office has agreed to release 80,000 yuan immediately and borrow 100,000 yuan from the bank jointly with the principals, totaling 180,000 yuan. The funds will be collected within a few days and handed over to the Education Fund Department for distribution to the schools. The remaining 60,000 yuan in arrears will be issued later. The principals are very satisfied with this result. After the funds are issued, they will leave Wuhu separately.

Hangzhou City's Education Budget for this Year 80

Provincial Funds Subsidize 70,000 Yuan

The Total for the Year is 340,000 Yuan

The Hangzhou City's Education Budget for the 19th year has been drafted. It is estimated that the total expenditure for the entire year, including the provisional and temporary fees, will be approximately 370,000 yuan. It has been submitted to the Education Department for review by the Provincial Committee. After discussion, it was submitted to the third and fourth meetings of the Provincial Committee. It was resolved to pass the budget in accordance with the review report, deducting over 34,000 yuan from the original budget, for a total of approximately 340,000 yuan. It has been determined. However, the city's education fees are significantly less than the expenditures. Therefore, it was resolved that the province would increase the subsidy by 70,000 yuan this year. The provincial government instructed the Hangzhou City Government yesterday. According to the report from the Education Department, the case of reviewing the Hangzhou City's Education Budget for the 19th year after being ordered to do so was presented at the 343rd meeting of the Government Committee and was resolved to pass the Education Budget for the 19th year in accordance with the review report and to approve an increase in the subsidy of 70,000 yuan this year. It is noted that this case was previously submitted by the city government and was resolved at the 334th meeting of the Government Committee to instruct the Education Department to review the city's Education Budget for the 19th year first and then approve it. It was also recorded and distributed to the city government and the Education Department. Now, according to the report on the previous situation and the previous resolution, in addition to instructing the Education Department and distributing it to the Finance Department for compliance, the city government is instructed to inform it of this order with the original review report.

Sports

North China Games 87

Postponement Possible Due to Cold Weather: Shenyang Correspondence: Zhang Xueliang, attaching importance to the North China Games, recently appointed Liu Fengzhu and others as members of the committee to prepare for the North China Games to be held in Liaoning. At 4:00 PM on September 30th, the preparatory committee members held a meeting at the Xinggong Education Association to discuss the arrangements. Those present were Wu Jiaxiang, Liu Fengzhu, Feng Yong, Sun Guofeng, Wang Zhaochu, Yao Jinsheng, Wang Huayi, Wang Zhuoran, Hao Gengsheng, Li Mengxing, Yan Yuheng, Chen Liyang, Li Shutang, and Li Jingcheng, totaling fourteen people. First, Wu Jiaxiang proposed that the North China Games should cooperate with the First Northeast Four Provinces Joint Games, but due to the cold weather and time constraints, it was not possible to hold them separately. Then, Wang Zhuoran proposed that this North China Games be suspended due to insufficient preparation time. Then, Wang Huayi proposed that the North China Games be added to the Northeast Joint Games and that the provinces be notified to participate. Those who have participated in the National Games can join the senior division. Then, Feng Yong proposed that due to the cold weather, accommodation, and curriculum issues, it could be considered to hold them in two phases. Then, Liu Fengzhu proposed that the name be changed to the Northeast Four Provinces Sponsored North China Games. Then, Yao Jinsheng proposed that the education departments of the North China provinces be telegraphed to instruct the schools to join the First Northeast Four Provinces Joint Games. The above proposals were discussed by the committee members due to time and type constraints, and five measures were formulated to request instructions from Zhang Xueliang: (1) The North China Games should be postponed due to the cold weather, short time, and lack of preparations, such as if the two sports meetings in the Northeast and North China are held together, it will delay the students' curriculum too much, it is best to postpone the North China Games. (2) If two meetings are held, the name is difficult to determine and disputes are likely to arise. Even if both parties negotiate, it is not possible to resolve it in a short period of time. (3) If the meeting is postponed for a week, it is feared that the education in the provinces will not be able to notify the schools in time, and the athletes have already set off. (4) If the superiors must order the holding of the China Games, the Northeast Joint Games will send a letter to Tianjin, Qingdao, and other places, inviting them to join the performance. (5) If the Northeast Joint Games are held first and the China Games are held a week later, it will greatly affect the students' studies and be economically difficult. The above five measures were recommended by the committee members to Feng Yong, Wu Jiaxiang, and Wang Huayi to meet Zhang Xueliang at 8:00 PM that night to request instructions on how to proceed.

Shanghai Third National Goods Movement Fair 97

Opening Ceremony Held at 2 PM Today

Fashion Exhibition on the 9th

Preparations for the Shanghai Third National Goods Movement Fair:

As reported in previous newspapers, the opening ceremony is scheduled to be held at 2 PM today at the National Goods United Department Store on Nanjing Road (formerly the site of the Municipal Government). The association has notified all sectors in advance to enthusiastically participate and contribute to the grand event. This fair is expected to be more enthusiastic than the previous two, with a superior location, many guests, shocking and inspiring displays, and excellent entertainment performances scheduled daily.

Comparing Years 17 and 18, imports increased for cotton goods, cotton, flour, chemicals, metals, minerals, machinery, lumber, synthetic indigo, dyes, and colors. Imports decreased for wool fabrics, silk fabrics, kerosene, candles, coal, meat products, tobacco, and cigarettes. This shows that our country's industry is progressing in an orderly manner, hence the increased imports of machinery, metals, lumber, indigo, and dyes, with machinery being particularly prominent. However, cotton and flour still heavily rely on foreign countries, and cotton imports remain above 200 million yuan annually, which is cause for some pessimism. The sharp decrease in imports of tobacco leaves, cigarettes, meat products, wool fabrics, and silk fabrics, especially silk fabrics, indicates that the Chinese people are living more rationally, which can be attributed to the National Goods Movement. We should continue to work hard to promote and advance the movement. We do not necessarily hope for a complete shift from import surplus to export surplus, but we hope that daily necessities and items that we already produce will no longer rely on imports. For example, replacing the 200 million yuan worth of imported foreign cloth with domestically produced cotton or silk fabrics is a deep hope for the near future. Performances will be held to add to the enjoyment, and famous people will give speeches to awaken the public. In addition, the National Goods Fashion Exhibition at the Dahua Hotel on the 9th is an unprecedented event in Shanghai. Many socialites are enthusiastically participating, and there will be a men's fashion show to enhance the event. During the preparation period, the association collected many contemporary writings and compiled a fair publication, which is bound into a volume, beautifully printed, rich in content, and of great research value. It will also be distributed to guests at the venue today. Details of each aspect are listed below:

Fair Declaration: Time does not stay, years pass like water. The Shanghai National Goods Movement Fair is now in its third session. Looking back over the past three years, the call to promote national goods has spread throughout the country, which is gratifying to those who participate in this event. However, in reality, no one can give a definitive answer to the questions of how much the production of national goods has increased and by how much the consumption of national goods has expanded. A review of customs trade registers reveals evidence to the contrary.

Net Value of Imported Foreign Goods (Customs Taels) Import Surplus (Customs Taels)

Today's National Goods Movement has even greater significance. Since the trend of expensive gold and cheap silver, the world economic situation has formed two trends. Countries using gold, especially those with developed industries, face fears of commercial decline and increased unemployment, and are urgently seeking to develop foreign markets to save their domestic crises. Countries using silver, especially those with nascent industries, suffer from rising prices and the hardship of living, and must be diligent and thrifty, develop their industries, and maintain a balance of foreign trade to survive. Today, among the silver-using countries in the world, who else but our country, with its vast territory and large population, can be exploited by capitalism? The so-called Far East Economic Survey Group is expected to arrive in droves, and the surplus goods of England, America, and Japan will compete fiercely in our country's market. If people are planning against us so thoroughly, then how should we plan for ourselves? In the past six months, the sharp fall in the price of silver has caused drastic changes in the national economy. Alarming words have arisen like bees, causing panic and astonishment. The people's concern and the government's dedication have never been greater. From top to bottom, we are united in seeking to restore the price of silver. Although there are different opinions and plans, repeated debates, and irresolvable questions, one point is unanimously agreed upon: to save on the waste of life in order to increase the happiness of individuals and society. In other words, to use national goods and reject luxury in order to develop our country's industry. All obstacles to the elimination and development of industry, such as the complete abolition of transit taxes, convenient transportation, and labor-management cooperation, are being formulated and gradually implemented by the central government's competent departments. The China Industrial and Commercial Management Association was also established in Shanghai at this time and will seek to rationalize the industry in terms of production technology and organization, in order to supply the market with a large quantity of inexpensive and high-quality goods, and increase the standard of living for the people. However, this matter is of great importance and requires the cooperation of the entire society. So, where does cooperation come from? Mr. He Jingzhi, in his speech on the frugality movement at the Central Party Headquarters on February 3 of this year, said, "...Developing industry cannot be achieved in a short time, so now we can only adopt passive methods to resist, and frugality is the only practical and effective method. All imported luxury goods should be rejected, and daily necessities that can be saved should be saved as much as possible. If there are national goods that can be substituted, then national goods must be used. In this way, the sales of foreign goods in China will be blocked, and imperialism will inevitably be greatly hit." His words are simple and easy to implement, and the great cause of saving the country lies within them. The association held its first meeting in July of the seventeenth year and declared to control waste and increase production, and called for economic hardship and a national salvation movement. Today, the crisis is a hundred times greater than it was the year before. Fellow patriots, repeat Mr. He's words, practice them diligently, and make them known to every household. Parents encourage their children, siblings, sisters-in-law, and daughters-in-law encourage each other, never forgetting them. Difficulty can revitalize the country. This is a golden opportunity to eliminate economic aggression and develop domestic industry, which will be fleeting and regrettable. The rise and fall of the country depend on this one move. As the third National Goods Movement Fair opens in this city, I offer a few words to the people:

Inscriptions by Celebrities: "The Shanghai Municipal Government will hold the Third National Goods Movement Week and the National Goods Fashion Fair at the same time during the Nineteenth National Day, and will issue a special publication, seeking words from me. I believe that Shanghai is a major trading port in our country, with railways and roads converging, and scholars and women gathering. The temporary habits are related to the views and hearings of all directions. Now, in the midst of promoting national goods, a fashion exhibition will be held. It will be seen that the tools for dressing and the items for decoration do not value foreign objects, but compete to admire national products. Changing customs, the country will follow, which is not difficult to predict at this meeting. Therefore, I will write a few words to express my praise, 'In the suburbs of Shanghai, bustling with activity, this grand event is a national glory. Collecting the best, displaying the finest, using it as a model, and collecting fashion widely, establishing a reputation, broadcasting it far and wide, the grand plan is covered, the people are prosperous and healthy, the duties are to benefit, and the expectations are great, the words are to celebrate, and Meng Jin is boundless, October of the Nineteenth Year, Kong Xiangxi.'" Wang Jiazhen Returns to Shanghai 98

A section official will temporarily remain in Weihai.

Mr. Wang is scheduled to depart for the capital by train this morning.

Mr. Wang Jiazhen, the Permanent Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, who was appointed as the commissioner for the reception of Weihaiwei, departed from Shanghai on the 27th of last month to Weihai to handle the reception matters. Having completed the task, he returned to Shanghai yesterday afternoon aboard the Dalian Maru, accompanied by his staff, including Guang Lin and Cui Cunlin. The ship was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at around 3:00 PM yesterday, but due to the sudden death of a passenger onboard, customs inspection at the entrance of Wusong delayed its arrival until around 4:00 PM. A reporter from the New Sound Society visited Mr. Wang at his residence on Route Massenet last night, and the following is a record of Mr. Wang's remarks:

Reception Process: The port of Weihai was received on the morning of the 1st. All properties in the area, as well as customs, salt affairs, judicial, postal, and telegraph services, have been completely received. I have separately handed them over to the receiving personnel dispatched by the respective responsible authorities to Weihai. The British Minister to Weihaiwei, Johnston, and the British Navy stationed on Liu Gong Island, all departed from the port on the afternoon of the 2nd. Due to the complexity of various affairs, Zhu Shiquan, Assistant of the European and American Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and section chiefs Ge Zukong and Fang Zobao, will temporarily remain in Weihai for ten days to assist Commissioner Xu Zushan in handling all matters.

British Municipal Administration: Weihai port has been leased to Britain for thirty-two years, covering an area of 2.81 million square feet, with a population of about 300,000. Through the British's determined management, the municipal administration is quite impressive. All buildings and land in the port are free from dilapidation and uncleanliness. The residents are plainly dressed, not flaunting wealth or luxury, nor are there any raggedly dressed people. The people live and work in peace and contentment, and there are very few lawsuits. Even when they meet in court, it is not difficult to resolve matters. There is a saying in the port, "The plaintiff summons the defendant, and the defendant will surely arrive." Inquiring about the facts, it is indeed true. In the event of a lawsuit, the judge first hears the plaintiff and then delivers the summons to the plaintiff to be served on the defendant. The defendant can appear in court on time. Furthermore, there are no weak horses in Weihai port, and horse-drawn carriages are not allowed to carry more than three people. Whenever a weak horse is found, the police immediately take it into custody and feed it for a period of ten days to fatten it up. The original owner then pays five jiao per day and takes it away. If it is not claimed within the deadline, the horse is sold at auction. The proceeds from the auction, minus the five yuan for the ten days of expenses, are still given to the owner. Chickens and ducks are never carried upside down; they must be held under the arm when entering the market. The municipal administration in the past was like this, so the residents are all grateful to Johnston. They are naive and lack a national concept, which is also due to their direct experience in life.

Page 10

Weihai People's Petition: The British originally established a customs office in Weihai port, and all imports and exports were taxed at a rate of one percent of their value. Therefore, merchants cleverly transported goods from nearby areas, such as peanuts produced in Shandong, to be exported through the port. Since the reception, the Inspector General of Customs has dispatched a customs officer to the port, along with the customs supervisor from the Ministry of Finance. On the 2nd, they posted a notice dated the 29th of last month to investigate the inventory of the entire port. The citizens then elected representatives to petition me, requesting that Weihai port be opened as a tax-free port like Zhongshan Port. I explained that tax collection is uniform nationwide. Zhongshan Port differs slightly from other places because of its competitive relationship with Hong Kong, and Huludao because of Dalian. Weihai is near Qingdao and Yantai, which are operated by Chinese, so it cannot favor one over the other. If the tax

rate is gradually increased by one level, I can convey this to the central government on their behalf. The citizens were satisfied.

On Liu Gong Island: Liu Gong Island is where Ding Jingshan, the naval admiral of the late Qing Dynasty, died for his country. Therefore, there are still many relics from that time. However, after the British operated it, they also invested in acquiring the land for public ownership, and it has become a paradise. In the future, during the hot season, the British and British troops will still be allowed to take refuge there. Institutions such as the British Naval Club, hospitals, and hotels are still operated by the British.

A Ship Stays in Weihai: The dispatch of warships to Weihai port was originally out of concern that disturbances might occur during the takeover or interference with municipal affairs. Therefore, warships were sent to the area to provide a deterrent. Currently, Hai Chen has carried me back to Qingdao. Zhen Hai and a part of the Marine Corps are still stationed in Weihai, and the order is very good. I am scheduled to return to the capital tomorrow morning (that is, this morning) to report my mission, he said.
