Telegram of Victory Received by the Garrison Department 100

Commander Xiong of Shanghai, for your information, our army has occupied Kaifeng, Jiang Yin respectfully informs you.

(Omissions) Our army began a general offensive against the rebellious enemy on the 5th of last month. The rebel Feng mobilized the main force and deployed it in the areas of Xuchang, Xinzheng, Changge, Zhengzhou, Rongyang, Mixian, Yuxian, and Luoyang, constructing solid fortifications to stubbornly resist. Our army, due to the courageous advance of the various subordinate columns, broke through the dangers and penetrated deeply. After more than ten days of fierce fighting, it had reached the vicinity of Xuchang, Zhengzhou, Rongyang, and Longmen Street south of Luoyang. The rebel enemy still relied on the fortresses, hoping to defend to the death. The morale of our various columns was a hundredfold, and the attack became even more urgent. According to reports, our troops on the railway front had defeated the troops of Tian Jinkai and Zhang Weixi on the morning of the Eastern date and occupied Xuchang. Approximately 40,000 troops under Song Tiancai and Jiao Wendian have surrendered one after another. Our army also captured a part of the rebel enemy's battalion of pistol teams, over a thousand rifles, and over a hundred pistols. Our Third Column has occupied the villages and fortresses seven or eight miles west of Zhengzhou, and the Fourth Column has occupied the area north of Rongyang Station. Our Fifth Column occupied Xicaodian on the Jiant day, and on the Eastern date, it occupied Baimasi east of Luoyang and Longmen Street south of Luoyang. The vanguard reached the vicinity of the western palace of Luoyang. The railway east of Luoyang was destroyed by us, and we are currently besieging Luoyang, which can be taken soon. Our Sixth Column is intercepting the defeated enemy to the north. At the same time, our Ninth Column occupied the areas of Caomiao, Maxuedian, and Mengzhuang, destroying the railway between Zhengzhou and Xinzheng. Our Second Column also occupied the areas of Changge and Heshangqiao, intercepting the return route and capturing two armored vehicles of the enemy. All columns have killed countless enemies one after another and captured many prisoners. It has been found that this battle was extremely fierce, lasting for ten days. Although the rebel enemy set up defenses at every step, resisting with all their might and holding on to the fortresses, they were eventually encircled and bravely defeated by our army. After this major blow, their hearts were filled with fear, and those who surrendered with weapons were still coming in an endless stream. At this moment, our various columns are still fiercely attacking Zheng and Luo, and the remaining enemies in Henan will be completely eliminated soon. I am submitting this report in advance. Liu Zhi, winter day.

Continuing Efforts in Anti-Drug Week 101

Strengthening the Race and Enriching the Country...Must First Reject Drugs

Today and yesterday are the last two days of the 7th National Anti-Drug Campaign Week. The situation is even more enthusiastic than before. Reports from provinces, cities, and counties across the country indicate that many people are actively participating in the movement. For example, in over four hundred places such as Changhua, Xiaoshan, Danyang, Changzhou, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Huzhou, Taixian, Ningbo, Nantian, Yixing, Chongde, Jiashan, Shanwu, Dinghai, Hangzhou, Suzhou, etc., in each city and county, the number of participating people often reaches several thousands. Detailed information about the enthusiastic activities in various places has been published in local newspapers, which shows the firm determination of our people to reject drugs. The situation of the past two days is summarized as follows: (1) Methods for Strengthening the Race Day A. Significance: In this era of the survival of the fittest, the survival of a race is determined by its prosperity or decline. The suffering of our country from opium poisoning is obvious and outrageous. The reason why our race is poor and weak today, and why we cannot ensure our survival from morning till night, is none other than the harm of opium. Therefore, if we want to revitalize the race, restore our original vigor, and strive to reject drugs, it is an urgent plan. B. Purpose: Anti-Drug Strengthening Race Day is to awaken compatriots to work hard to eliminate opium and narcotic drugs. Its purpose can be divided into three types: (A) To eliminate the planting, selling, and smoking of opium in the country; (B) To prevent the smuggling and sale of foreign opium and narcotic drugs; (C) To abolish the opium monopoly system specifically targeting overseas Chinese by colonial governments in Southeast Asia. C. Methods (1) Conduct a survey of narcotic drugs; (2) Publicize the tragic situation of international drug disasters in China; (3) Recruit individual members; (4) Organize anti-drug propaganda meetings; (5) Expose the opium monopoly policy of colonial governments in Southeast Asia that harms overseas Chinese; (6) Hold a grand anti-drug oath ceremony.

(2) Outline for Strengthening the Race Day Propaganda In recent years, our country's diplomacy has failed, internal affairs have not been properly managed, the national system is poor and weak, and people's lives are impoverished. The root cause is the spread of opium addiction, which is getting worse every day. If we continue like this without seeking remedies, it will inevitably lead to national subjugation and racial extinction. Since the opening of the sea ban, European, Near Eastern, and Japanese countries have continuously imported opium and all kinds of narcotics into our country, carrying out a planned invasion movement in the hope of achieving their goal of destroying our country and our race. Some people in our country are aware of their intentions, but without the support of the masses, their abilities are weak, and they cannot resist this aggressive force. Huang Juezi, a pioneer in rejecting drugs, submitted a memorial discussing the evils of opium, saying: "First, use the useful wealth of China to fill the endless ravines overseas; use this harmful thing to gradually become a national worry. Day after day, I don't know when it will end. Upon investigation, opium smoke is made in England, which strictly prohibits its own people from eating it, and specializes in enticing people from other countries to make them weak. They have already used this to take Ge Liuba, and now they want to entice Annam. Annam strictly prohibits it and it has finally been eliminated. Now it is spreading in China, estimating human figures, ruining people's wills, and losing people's wealth. It is a great disaster that has never been seen in the history of living beings. Its disaster is more severe than floods and wild beasts." His words are poignant and awaken people. The past poison of opium is a fact that exists. Now, let's add one or two more for our reference. The recent excessive manufacture of narcotics exceeds the use of medical drugs by thousands of times. According to the report of the British representative Mr. Malcolm at the International League's Opium Committee last spring, a certain Dutch pharmaceutical factory in Liaofa manufactured 955 kilograms of morphine, 3,040 kilograms of heroin, and 90 kilograms of cocaine, while the amount transported into our country was as much as 760 kilograms of morphine, 1,316 kilograms of heroin, and 40 kilograms of cocaine. This large amount of medicine is enough to poison more than 10 million people. A small fact can prove the fierceness of the drug disaster. There are currently more than 130 factories in the world that manufacture narcotic drugs, engaging in large-scale production to meet the needs of the Eastern market. The opium addiction in the country has already had a significant impact on national health. Can we tolerate the fact that in the Northeast and the Yellow River basin, foreigners are still engaged in drug trafficking? At present, the masses are being ravaged by drugs and are on the verge of death. The number is alarming. This is indeed a major problem facing our nation and cannot be ignored. Everyone knows that opium and narcotic drugs harm the human body, but without careful investigation and research, we will never know the extent of the harm. According to Dr. Du Congming, smokers shorten their lifespan by an average of 20 years. Most medical experts have proven that morphine addicts can die in 105 years, and heroin addicts can die in two years. Now the drug disaster is spreading and intensifying, and addicts are all over the country. How can the nation not be weakened? Colonial governments in Southeast Asia take aggressive measures against Chinese people. They strictly prohibit people of other races from smoking opium, and their purpose is not only in taxation. If we study it slightly, we can know that behind this aggressive action, there is actually a conspiracy to exterminate the race, which must be paid attention to. According to accurate statistics, in the British Malay Archipelago (including the Straits Settlements and the Malay Federation), at least 20% of overseas Chinese are addicted to opium. That is, among the 2 million overseas Chinese, 400,000 are addicted. The most affected are the working class. Most of the Chinese workers in the factories smoke opium. Similar phenomena also exist in the Dutch East Indies. The situation is more tragic than this. Most of the overseas Chinese only become addicted to opium after going to Southeast Asia. Those who bring it from China account for only two or three tenths. This fact was clearly announced by the Malay Government Opium Committee, and its authenticity is known. However, the British government, on the one hand, allows overseas Chinese to smoke opium, and on the other hand, prevents indigenous and European and American people from enjoying this right. There is nothing stranger than this. The British Malay government and the Dutch East Indies government both have clear orders prohibiting other people from buying opium except for Chinese people. What is the intention? According to the opinion of a representative at the Malay Opium Committee meeting (1923-1924), opium can poison other races, but if used in appropriate amounts, it will not poison Chinese people. According to medical experts related to the British government, opium is a good medicine for preventing and treating malaria and can prolong human life. This kind of specious and absurd argument is not worth a smile from knowledgeable people. We must know that the governments of various Southeast Asian colonies only allow Chinese people to smoke opium. Their purpose is not only in taxation, but also contains a conspiracy to exterminate the race. The facts are obvious and cannot be concealed. If we want to strengthen the country, we must first strengthen the race. If we want to strengthen the race, we must first get rid of this poisonous substance that exterminates the race. The goals of today's movement are: (1) Rejecting longevity to strengthen personal physique is the fundamental key. A race is formed by gathering individuals. Only when everyone is healthy can we create a completely healthy nation. (2) Rejecting drugs is to increase the health of people in society. A healthy society can move upward and not degenerate. (3) Rejecting drugs is to improve the ability of the nation to survive and struggle, so as not to be eliminated by nature. (4) Rejecting drugs is to eliminate all evil customs that harm the body and corrupt morals, and to protect the nation so that it can have the virtue of strength and health. (5) Rejecting drugs is to increase the production of materials and nature, so as to increase the food necessary for national health. (6) Rejecting drugs is to eliminate all obstacles that hinder national health.

(3) Holding Anti-Drug Speeches during Commemoration Week Yesterday was the day when various agencies and organizations held Commemoration Week. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association had requested the Municipal Party Headquarters to notify party headquarters at all levels to add anti-drug speeches and oaths during the Commemoration Week. The association specially distributed various publicity materials to party headquarters at all levels in the city for use in the event. The association also directly distributed the materials to various administrative agencies and organizations and requested them to handle the matter.

(4) Petitioning the Government to Issue a General Order for Annual Routine Anti-Drug Week The National Anti-Drug Campaign Week has been held in various places for seven sessions. In the first three sessions, it was purely a separate movement of the masses. In the latter four sessions, most local government agencies participated one after another, especially during this session, which was even more intense. This is because at this time, the prohibition of opium was being relaxed. The people in various places were determined to hold anti-drug campaigns, and enthusiastic groups in various places also regarded the importance of the opium prohibition issue, so most of them also participated. This is indeed a good phenomenon in the anti-drug campaign. In the future, this spirit should be expanded and continued to make compatriots in various places understand the importance and urgency of the opium prohibition administration. The anti-drug campaign should be regarded as a necessary auxiliary movement for the masses in the process of implementing opium prohibition. Not only should they take the lead in advocating it, but they should also hold it together with the local people on the scheduled date of Anti-Drug Week. In order to encourage administrative personnel in various places, the Ministry of Interior should formulate a national examination method. The association specially decided to submit a petition to the Ministry of Interior, ordering the civil affairs departments of various provinces to forward it to the governments of various cities and counties, from October 1st to 7th every year, to routinely carry out Anti-Drug Campaign Week according to the regulations of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, and to conduct practical assessments for rewards and punishments, and to publish this anti-drug date in the calendar to mark it and not forget it.

(5) Methods for the Enriching the Country Day Campaign (A) Significance: A rich country has strong people, and a poor country has weak people. This is a matter of course. The opium poison has harmed our country, ravaged the race, and hindered construction, causing the foundation of the country to shake and the people's lives to be in distress. The money lost by our country every year due to opium poisoning is countless. If this financial resource is used for construction, it will benefit the country in unlimited ways. Today, the fundamental remedy is to remove the obstacles to construction and quickly fill the leaks. Then the country's future may be saved. (B) Purpose: The purpose of the Anti-Drug Enriching the Country Day is to unite compatriots, unanimously reject drugs, promote domestic construction, and resist foreign poisons. (C) Methods (1) Hold anti-drug speeches at school morning meetings; (2) Student teams go out in four directions to promote anti-drug; (3) Hold student anti-drug speech or debate competitions; (4) Hold student anti-drug essay competitions; (5) Hold student anti-drug amusement galas; (6) Hold competitions to promote the sale of monthly publications; (7) Organize student anti-drug propaganda meetings; (8) Hold anti-drug oaths.

(6) Outline for the Enriching the Country Day Propaganda Opium and all kinds of narcotic drugs have harmed China for more than a day. It is not only a matter of economic deduction, but also the biggest reason for the increasing poverty of people's lives. From the middle of the Qing Dynasty to today, for more than a hundred years, the British have continuously transported a large amount of Indian and Persian opium into China, exchanging it for tens of thousands of taels of silver to go. If we estimate that China buys foreign goods for 25 million taels every year, then in the past 100 years, it has been 2.5 trillion taels. China has suffered this huge loss in the recent 100 years of national poverty and financial exhaustion. How can we imagine the impact on the national economy? In the past 20 years, in addition to opium, there have also been narcotic drugs transported from various countries in the East and West, such as morphine, heroin, cocaine, red and white pills, etc. The value is ten times that of opium. The amount is even more immeasurable. The country's consumption is increasing and the leaks are getting bigger every day. This is something to be noted. (1) Nearly 8 million overseas Chinese live on islands in Southeast Asia. The families of these overseas Chinese remit money every month to support their lives. However, for many years, the powers have vigorously implemented a drug policy in the islands of Southeast Asia and Indochina, enticing overseas Chinese to become addicted to drugs and collecting huge taxes every year. It is pitiful that ignorant overseas Chinese have since fallen into the black register from which they can never recover. The income from hard work every day is used for food, clothing, and smoking, and they are still worried that it is not enough. Let alone remit money back to the country and mail it to their relatives. If we estimate that 30% of all overseas Chinese are smokers, then the money that should be remitted back to the motherland every year is swallowed by the colonial governments of the powers. How can the amount not be surprising? The impact on the national economy can be imagined. This is something to be noted. (2) Since the fifth year of the Republic of China, wars have been frequent and the opium prohibition in various provinces has been extremely chaotic. Corrupt local bullies have risen up to deceive rural farmers and plant poppies. In the provinces of Shaanxi, Gansu, Sichuan, Guizhou, and recently in northern Anhui and southern Fujian, opium seedlings are all over the ground and are endless. Farmers already know the benefits of growing opium, so they have followed each other in abandoning grain and planting this poisonous substance, resulting in frequent famines in the provinces along the river in northern Jiangsu. There is no grass in the fields, and the five grains are not harvested. The disaster of civil unrest and the dead bodies of refugees are everywhere, and the red earth is thousands of miles. The seriousness of the disaster and the magnitude of the impact can be told by anyone who pays a little attention to current affairs. The southeastern provinces, which are known for their wealth, have always transported rice and grain to East Asia. In recent years, there has been a shortage of grain. They have had to buy rice and grain from Siam and Annam. The amount of leakage every year is unimaginable. Although the reasons for this are not the same, the planting of opium in many provinces is indeed a step towards disaster. Its direct and indirect impact on the national economy is extremely large. This is something to be noted. (3) In the past 20 years, the drug situation has gradually expanded. There are farmers who plant opium, workers who manufacture opium, merchants who sell opium, smugglers who transport opium, and smokers who smoke opium. Recently, there are also officials who specialize in opium, military police who crack down on smuggling, local gentry who contract donations, and local tyrants who protect rural farmers. All of the above, in various forms, rely on opium for their livelihoods. They even use illegal powers to collect money as the opium prohibition is opened. If we count the people who are directly and indirectly related to opium, there are probably tens of millions in the country. Most of the families of these tens of millions of people have fallen into the black box. This is also an expected event. These tens of millions of useful people do not engage in legitimate occupations, but use illegal poisonous substances to collect money. How can the impact on the national economy be imagined? This is something to be noted. (4) In this eventful century in which China is located, the national industry and commerce has been in a state of depression due to foreign economic aggression. Moreover, due to the direct and indirect squeeze of opium and narcotic drugs, the people's livelihood has fallen into a desperate situation. This is indeed something that must be paid attention to. China was originally an economically backward country, so how can it permanently follow this disaster? For the plan now, all of our people and anti-drug comrades should know that enriching the country is the only way to save the people's livelihood in China. The phenomenon of today's stagnation is caused by opium. If we can rise up and unite all the people in the country to reject drugs and eliminate all opium and narcotic drugs, and use the money spent on opium to construct the country, such as revitalizing education and developing transportation, then the people's livelihood can become increasingly prosperous, and the wealth of China can be expected. Opium and narcotic drugs were originally a drug policy implemented by the powers against us. If we do not think of vigorously resisting it, what will be the consequences? Rejecting drugs is a necessary method for enriching the country. There is no doubt about it. I hope that all the people in the country will pay attention to it three times.

(7) Promoting the Construction of the Lin Zexu Memorial Hall During the commemoration of the national humiliation agreement on June 3rd this year, all sectors of Shanghai decided to build the Lin Zexu Memorial Hall in Shanghai to trace the past and encourage the future. A preparatory committee has been formed to be responsible for the preparation and progress of the work, which has been reported in previous newspapers. The association intends to promote the early success of the memorial hall during this Anti-Drug Week. The memorial hall preparatory committee has decided to proceed with various plans as soon as possible, and to establish the Shanghai Memorial Hall as soon as possible so that provinces, cities, and counties can continue to hold activities.

(8) Proposal to Establish an International Anti-Drug Alliance In recent years, our country has suffered from the harm of domestic opium planting and the tea poison of foreign narcotic drugs. The situation is tragic and unbearable. Since its establishment, the association has done its best to fight, and has achieved many results. Judging from today's situation, domestic opium prohibition has not been effectively implemented and does not rely on public opinion. The manufacture of foreign drugs cannot be stopped by our country alone. As for the concessions and leased territories, as well as foreign rogues, they are all obstacles to our country's opium prohibition. It is impossible to deal with this difficult and complex problem without the strength of countries that sympathize with the national system. Sympathetic groups in European and American countries have repeatedly requested cooperation from the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, requesting that the people of our country, who have suffered the most, initiate the establishment of an International Anti-Drug Alliance to strengthen momentum and increase strength. At the association's fifth annual meeting, the Combined National Body Overseas Chinese Affairs Advancement Association made the same suggestion. Considering the situation, the anti-drug movement will either advance or retreat. It is difficult to achieve good results without further planning. The proposed methods are as follows, and are submitted for public decision: 1. The association will send letters to solicit opinions from European and American anti-drug groups, sympathetic groups, and enthusiastic leaders; 2. International groups, such as Christian churches, Catholic churches, women's alliances, and the Red Cross, should be contacted; 3. The association should send letters to foreign ambassadors and overseas Chinese leaders and groups to engage in assistance and advocacy in their resident countries in advance; 4. The association should send representatives to European and American countries to contact comrades and initiate the organization of this plan. The executive committee discussed the plan submitted by the secretariat and generally approved it. It was decided to appoint Wang Jingqi, Wu Liande, Ding Shujing, Cai Rudong, Guo Baoyi, Zhong Keto, Huang Jiawei, etc. to form a review committee to pass a detailed plan to be drafted by Wang Jingqi and Huang Jiawei.

(9) Foreign Groups Send Letters Requesting Cooperation The American White Cross Anti-Drug Association, knowing that our country's 7th National Anti-Drug Week is being held this year, has sent a letter expressing its willingness to cooperate. The letter reads in part: "I have read the letter from Chief Secretary Huang of the Shanghai Chinese National Anti-Drug Association. The association is working hard to reject drugs and attaches importance to international work. It is very willing to expand the scope of this movement and cooperate with foreign groups. Our colleagues will follow and work hard." Other groups, such as the anti-opium association founded by the Dutch in Batavia and the World Anti-Drug Education, have also sent many letters with similar meanings, which will not be repeated.

(10) Airplanes Distribute Leaflets The Navy dispatched airplanes to distribute more than 200,000 leaflets in the air. For a time, snowflakes flew. The leaflets were rectangular and contained a picture of a life-and-death juncture, the date of the 7th Anti-Drug Week, and an oath. It is said that if the oath form of this leaflet is filled in with the name and a four-cent postage stamp is mailed to the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road, a copy of the excellent anti-drug publication will be presented. (11) Recent Statistics on the Opium Disaster Among Overseas Chinese In British Malaya, in 1929, the total number of imported opium was 3,843 boxes. The total weight of opium sold to Singapore was 3,037,272 taels. There were a total of 65 opium selling places, including 31 in Singapore, 20 in Penang, 12 in Malacca, 1 in Nakan, and 1 in Christmas Island. The total consumption of opium for the year was 1,152,196 taels. The total income was 14,804,769 yuan (more than 14 million yuan). 1,857,536 taels were transported from Singapore and Penang to the interior of the Malay Federation. As for the number of registered smokers, it was 40,956. Among them, foreign smokers accounted for 93 Indians and 40 Malays. The remaining 40,823 were overseas Chinese from the provinces of Fujian and Guangdong in our country. The total income from opium was 12,938,721 yuan.

Cancellation of the Jin Song Qing Ping Bandit Suppression Temporary Command Post 102

The bandit leader Tai Bao A Shu has fled to the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui. Xiong Shihui, the commander-in-chief of bandit suppression in the three provinces, previously appointed Hu Zhengji as the temporary commander of bandit suppression in Jin (shan), Song (jiang), Qing (pu), and Ping (hu), and ordered the suppression to be completed by the end of September. The establishment of the temporary command was originally intended to specifically suppress the bandit Tai Bao A Shu. Recently, because the bandit leader has been repeatedly suppressed by the military police of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces in the Taihu, Dianshan Lake, Dazheng Mountain, and Xiaozheng Mountain areas, they have all fled. Therefore, the temporary commander Hu Zhengji submitted a special request to the general command headquarters the day before yesterday to temporarily cancel the bandit suppression temporary command headquarters. His original request stated in part: "Your department was ordered to suppress bandits, and has supervised the army and police day and night to search and suppress in separate routes. Recently, it was found that after the bandit Tai Bao A Shu was suppressed, his entire bandit gang has indeed been dispersed. A small number have fled back to the Jinping area and have also changed their tactics, decentralizing themselves and hiding in rural villages to avoid the eyes and ears of the government. With such a small number of vagrant bandits, it is not only difficult for the military police to capture them, but even the local people do not know their whereabouts. Moreover, the counties are holding a cleaning campaign, so the bandit suppression temporary command headquarters can be temporarily cancelled. The bandit suppression troops, with one company stationed in each of the two counties, assist the water police in searching and suppressing and handling the cleaning campaign," etc. Now Commander-in-Chief Xiong has approved the cancellation.

Request to Revoke the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Rice Export Ban 103

The Municipal Government submitted a document to the Executive Yuan. The Municipal Government submitted a document to the Executive Yuan stating: "It is submitted for consideration. According to the report submitted by Pan Gongzhan, the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, the Rice Food Committee of the city submitted a report stating: At the 18th regular meeting of your committee, Commissioner Cai Yukun made a temporary motion that because the export of Zhejiang rice is banned, the price of rice is lower than that in Shanghai. Farmers will have difficulty selling their new rice at a good price and will inevitably be disappointed. Moreover, because Jiangsu and Zhejiang are intertwined, it is appropriate to allow circulation. Please forward the matter for handling. It was decided to forward the matter to the National Government to reiterate the ban on hoarding rice and allow free circulation in various places, but strictly prohibit private exports overseas to feed the people. Please review and forward," etc. In view of this, the domestic rice circulation has already been governed by the National Government’s General Order. This Zhejiang province rice export ban, we assume, is because Zhejiang rice has never been self-sufficient and should leave a surplus to prepare for a shortage. Also, they may be afraid that after the rice is exported, it will be smuggled overseas. Its aim is probably similar to the ban on the export of Jiangsu rice. However, Jiangsu and Zhejiang are interconnected and intertwined. To transport Zhejiang rice into Zhejiang, it must pass through Jiangsu territory. To transport Jiangsu rice into Jiangsu, it must pass through Zhejiang territory. If each other issues a ban, they will lose the benefits of circulation. Farmers are eager to sell goods, but they are afraid of congestion. Merchants take advantage of their failings to suppress their values. Although there is a reality of a good harvest, the gains are no different from a famine year. At this time, silver has fallen and all things are expensive, but agricultural products are uniquely cheap. How can farmers survive? To prevent smuggling overseas, it is necessary to jointly enforce the sea ban and rectify customs. It is not the business of various provinces to obstruct the flow of rice between themselves. Therefore, to maintain the people's food supply in the present situation, we must first transfer the surplus to the deficit to maintain a reasonable price of rice and grain, so that farmers do not damage their capital and merchants do not lose their profits. Only then can the treacherous merchants have no hope for illegal gains from smuggling overseas. If the price of rice falls due to the blockade of the territory, the treacherous merchants will come up with all sorts of tricks. The ports of Jiangsu and Zhejiang are different, and the sea ban is slightly sparse. Smuggling is inevitable. If there is a consideration of the pain of foreign rice imports and the outflow of money in past years, we should think about a rainy day and plan for the safety of the people's food supply in the country. We should follow the legacy of Changping to restore warehousing. The fundamental plan is nothing more than this. Prohibiting exports will only make matters more complicated. It is difficult to expect a good result. It will only make farmers and merchants miserable and will not benefit the people's livelihood. Given the previous situation, may we ask your government to forward the matter to the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to revoke the order banning the export of rice and grain and jointly strictly prevent smuggling at the seaports? Or may we forward the matter to the Executive Yuan for review and instruct them to comply? We submit this document for your review and instructions for compliance." In view of this, smuggling rice and grain overseas should be strictly prohibited. As for the provinces, if the export of rice is uniformly prohibited and circulation is mutually obstructed, not only will farmers and merchants be困, but also the future of the people's food supply will be greatly affected. The matters reported by the bureau are not without merit. In addition to the instructions, we submit this document for your review and prompt instructions to the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to revoke the measures banning the export of rice, and at the same time, we should pay more attention to preventing smuggling at the seaports to feed the people, which is indeed a public convenience.

A Kidnapping Case Cracked on the Songshan Maru

The Songshan Maru steamer docked at the Yangjiadu pier in Pudong the day before yesterday. Kidnapper Gu A Da and others were found to have kidnapped three boys, intending to sell them in Xiamen and Hong Kong. Before the boat had set sail, a detective from the First District of the Water Police Force received a report from an informant and went to investigate. The kidnappers Gu A Da, Jiang Guo Ren, Ji Lan Sheng, Zhou A Mao, Tian Xiao Heshang, Wang Rui Rong, Gu Han Lin, and a woman Xu Zhou Shi were caught on the spot, along with the kidnapped boys Du Lin Fang, Li Zhan Fang, and Hua A Di. They were immediately sent to the First District Headquarters. After interrogation, they confessed to the kidnapping and trafficking without denial. Zhou A Mao, only nineteen years old, was also a kidnapper, specializing in acting like a child and luring children into their trap. Zhou also confessed that Zhou A Gen, living at No. 195 Runde Lane, Huanghe Road in the French Concession, provided the kidnappers' hideout. The district immediately dispatched detectives accompanied by the police to arrest Zhou A Gen and rescued two more kidnapped boys, Zhu You Quan and Wang Xiao San, who were taken to the headquarters. The case has been clarified, and the kidnapped boys will be kept for their families to claim them. If there are no family members, they will be sent to the relief association for care. The gang of kidnappers was sent to the local court for investigation yesterday.

Japanese Ship Sinks Stone Boat

The Ryusbo Maru, a Japanese merchant ship of the Nisshin Company, was importing goods into Shanghai from overseas at 6:45 p.m. the night before last. As it approached the Pudong surface near the China Merchants Bureau's Central Pier, it encountered a pier boat owned by Dai Kai Fa, loaded with 52 tons of stones, sailing downstream. The Japanese ship was traveling very fast, and due to careless steering, it crashed head-on into the stone boat, causing it to rupture and sink to the bottom of the river along with its cargo. Eight boatmen fell into the water at the same time. Six were rescued with great effort, but two remain missing and are presumed drowned. It is reported that the loss of the boat and cargo is significant, and the cargo owner is preparing to negotiate with the offending shipping company to claim compensation.

Died from Taking Poison Due to Poverty

Zhang Cheng Quan, a 37-year-old man from Wuxi, made a living selling smoked sausages. He and his wife rented a garret at No. 8 Dongxin Lane, Maidie An Road (formerly Xinjie) in the French Concession. His wife suffered a difficult childbirth a month ago and was sent to the Maternity Hospital. After the doctor performed a surgery to deliver the baby, Zhang's wife died due to weakness. Zhang managed to arrange the funeral. On the 5th of this month, which was the seventh week after his wife's death, Zhang, due to poverty and gambling losses, became despondent and took his own life by swallowing raw opium in the morning. After taking the poison, he lay down to die. When the poison took effect and he moaned, his roommate Chen Bing Rong and the sub-landlord found out and took Zhang to Renji Hospital. However, the poisoning was too severe, and he died at 2 p.m. that afternoon. The hospital notified the Grand Self-Ringing Bell Police Station, which sent detectives to take the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall for an autopsy. The detectives found that the deceased had no family. The detectives reported this to the head detective and are awaiting an autopsy today. The deceased's friends are preparing clothing and a coffin and will arrange for burial after the examination.

An Elderly Man Died of Anxiety from Unsuccessful Debt Collection

Zhu Chun San, the owner of the Zhu Chun Ji Rice Shop outside the South City Bund in this city, was nearly sixty years old. Before the Mid-Autumn Festival, he went to Nanjing with his son to collect debts. Unexpectedly, a debtor owed over five thousand taels of silver and went into hiding. Because Zhu could not collect the debt, he was extremely anxious and burst into tears. He became ill due to anxiety, and his son helped him onto a train to Wang Zi Ming's house, his relative in Nanguang outside the North Gate of Wuxi, to rest temporarily and seek medical treatment. However, Zhu was old and weak and could not bear the worry and anxiety, and he died the day before yesterday. His son urgently telegraphed his mother in Wuxi yesterday to take a train to Wuxi to arrange the funeral. This is truly a tragic incident amidst the debt collection at the end of September.

A Madman Laughs and Cries

Yesterday afternoon around 3 p.m., a man suddenly appeared in the Dongjiadu area of the South City, walked near the Bund, and jumped into the Huangpu River when people were unprepared. Li Chang Yong, a guard on duty at the 16th post, saw this and rushed to rescue him, saving his life. When asked why he jumped into the river to die, he spoke incoherently, as if mentally disturbed. He was taken back to the First Section of the First District Police Station. When the section chief interrogated him, asking his name and address, he suddenly laughed up to the sky, and when asked why, he suddenly lowered his head and cried incessantly. Since he seemed to be a madman, there was no way to investigate further. He was instructed to prepare a document to report to the Municipal Police Bureau to request placement.

An Ungrateful Friend and a Shameless Wife

Li Zhen Fu Repaid Kindness with Evil

Li Zhen Fu, a 33-year-old man from Haizhou, worked as a laborer and lived on Wanyu Street in the South City. His wife, Zhang, was 21 years old and had a reputation for being flirtatious. Li had a friend, Zhou Ke Shun, a 29-year-old man from Siyang, who was unemployed and struggling financially. He was also suffering from illness. Li took pity on him and allowed him to stay at his home temporarily, providing food and lodging for him to recuperate. Yesterday afternoon, Li went out on business. Around 2 p.m., he suddenly returned home to get something. Unexpectedly, he stepped into the bedroom and saw Zhou Ke Shun and his wife, Zhang, both naked in bed. Li was extremely angry at this situation, as he had shown kindness only to be betrayed. He immediately rushed forward to restrain them. The man and woman had already realized they were discovered and jumped out of bed to put on clothes and try to escape. Li ran out and called for help from Liang Jin Hai, a guard on duty at the 8th post, who took both of them to the First Section of the First District Police Station. After a preliminary interrogation by the section chief, they were ordered to be detained separately for further investigation.

Ruan Wu Shao Receives an Extortion Letter

Ruan Mu Bo, also known as Ruan Wu Shao, a native of Jiangdu residing at No. 13 Huanlong Lane, West Messerti Road, French Concession, is the direct grandson of the former Qing Dynasty Yangzhou Grand Tutor Ruan. He is known for being sociable, generous, and charitable. Everyone in the Huaiyang area knows Ruan Wu Shao. Li Jing Lin, the former Zhili Governor, was one of Mr. Ruan's sworn friends. (Mr. Ruan is the fifth child, and people respect him by calling him Wu Shao.) Although he is over sixty years old, due to his wide social circle and lack of permanent property, he is always busy running a business to make a living. Unexpectedly, he recently received an extortion letter demanding 5,000 yuan. The words in the letter were extremely aggressive. Mr. Ruan laughed it off. Yesterday, he mentioned it to friends and relatives, and onlookers were outraged and strongly urged him to report it to the police for a thorough investigation. However, Mr. Ruan is naturally kind and stopped them, hoping the perpetrators would reform. It is reported that he vacated the house in Huanlong Lane yesterday, auctioned off the furniture, and returned to Jiangdu to recuperate.

A Young Woman Swallows Opium for a Gold Ring

Dies from Lack of Medical Treatment

Zhang A Feng, a 17-year-old young woman from Ningbo, lived at No. 12 Songbai Lane, Baxianqiao, French Concession. Her husband worked for a tobacco company. Yesterday afternoon, she wanted to exchange a gold ring, but her husband refused, causing an argument. Depressed, she secretly swallowed raw opium. When people noticed, she was rushed to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, the opium poison attacked her heart, and she died around 8 p.m. due to lack of treatment.

Kunshan Painting Theft Case

The victim Xu Wu Qi, who lived at the Laifu Hall on Dongtang Street in Kunshan, was a well-known local gentry and a lover of antiques and famous paintings. Xu passed away this spring. During the funeral in March, Wu Meng Chang and Wu Kang Hou, brothers from Taiping Bridge in the same county, conspired with Yao Long Hai's son, Gen Quan (a carpenter), to steal over a hundred pieces of valuable paintings and antiques from Xu's house. Among them were Tang Yin's "Hundred Birds Worshipping the Phoenix" and Wang Shigu's "Ten Thousand Miles of Yangtze River," worth about ten thousand taels of silver. The thief Yao Gen Quan hid the stolen goods in Wu Kang Hou's house without anyone knowing. After many days, someone secretly informed the Xu family, who immediately checked and found that the items had indeed been stolen. They immediately reported to the Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, requesting an investigation. Team Leader Wei Xu Chu immediately dispatched the entire team of detectives to arrest the suspects at their addresses. However, the thieves Yao Gen Quan and the Wu brothers had already fled with the stolen goods after hearing the news. Only Yao Gen Quan's father, Yao Long Hai, was arrested. The main suspects in this case are the Wu brothers, and Kang Hou has considerable savings, claiming to have a hundred thousand taels. He is a shareholder in a sock factory on Main Street in the county and has sock factories in the British and French Concessions in Shanghai. Therefore, the Wu brothers fled to the Shanghai Concessions. The Public Security Bureau ordered Detective Team Leader Wei Xu Chu to prepare a document and send detectives Wang Yun Shan to Shanghai in July to cooperate with the Concession Police in the arrest, but they were not found. Later, Wu Kang Hou asked someone to mediate with the victim and returned ten famous paintings. However, half of the other items had already been sold and could not be returned, so the case was delayed until now. Unexpectedly, the Wu brothers are hiding in the Concessions, evading the law. It is recently heard that they have sold the paintings to a Westerner, and they have fallen into foreign hands. Therefore, the Xu family has again petitioned the Public Security Bureau to send detectives to Shanghai to investigate. It has been bought, and the line is being pursued.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Responds Regarding the Date of Dismissal of Shop Employees

Should Be Handled in Accordance with the Gregorian Calendar for Closing Accounts

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a report to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating: "Regarding the matter of submitting a draft of measures for the dismissal of employees in various industries in accordance with the order for review and approval. We found that we previously received Instruction No. 813 from your Bureau, instructing us to conduct a detailed investigation into whether there were any obstacles after changing the hiring and dismissal of shop employees in various industries to be in accordance with the Gregorian calendar and to draft implementation measures to be reported for approval. After forwarding this to various industry guilds for review and reply, we subsequently received replies from over forty guilds, including those for miscellaneous grains, oil cakes, bean rice, silk fabrics, sauce gardens, Chinese medicine, liquor, and pawnshops. The majority requested that, in accordance with past customs and the Gregorian calendar, the end of May, the end of September, and the end of December be the dates for closing accounts for the three festivals, which would also be the dates for dismissal of employees in various industries. Although there were occasional cases where the standard was the peak or off-season of business, or dismissals occurred in February, August, May, or December, or only once at the end of each year, these were only a minority. We submitted the habits of various industries in their replies to the Labor-Management Issues Research Committee of the Association for detailed review. The review results indicated that the old habits of employee hiring and dismissal were generally based on the three festivals each year. Now that the Gregorian calendar is being implemented, the majority opinion of various industries should be followed, with the end of May, the end of September, and the end of December of the Gregorian calendar each year being the dates for the dismissal of employees. However, in the event of major incidents, temporary dismissals may be made. The Pen and Ink Industry Guild raised concerns about calculating the delayed dismissal of employees by one month according to the Gregorian calendar, as ordered. We believe that this proposed delay is specifically for debt contracts, and it seems inappropriate to apply it to employee hiring and dismissal. The closing of accounts for shops is inherently linked to the hiring and dismissal of employees. If the calculation is changed to be delayed by one month according to the Gregorian calendar, the shop's profit and loss and business expansion and contraction would mostly become things of the past, and there would be no need to hire or dismiss employees. From the perspective of the employees themselves, the dismissal date would have passed, and the hiring and dismissal of employees in various shops would have been finalized, making it impossible to switch to other shops. Both parties would feel inconvenienced, and there is indeed room for correction." This was raised for discussion at the 14th Standing Committee meeting of the Association on the 2nd of this month. It was deemed that the results of the review took into account laws, customs, business conditions, and other aspects and could serve as an appropriate method of dismissal after the adoption of the Gregorian calendar. It was resolved to submit this to your Bureau for review and instruction. It is appropriate to prepare a document to submit for review and to be given instructions to follow, as it would be in the public interest.

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau's Grain Statistics

January to August

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau released grain statistics for this year, stating that the rice price this year increased from February after poor harvests in various regions last year. The price even reached over ten yuan the following month, and the average price of japonica rice reached 20 yuan and 5 cents. Starting in May, the Bureau began registering rice boats and evaluating prices. When there was a shortage of goods, the average price of high-priced rice was distributed to various rice shops to avoid competition and eliminate hidden discounts. In July, new grain entered the market, and a bumper harvest was expected, and the price gradually fell. In September, new rice flooded in, and the decline will be even more drastic. Amidst the high rice prices, the Bureau presented to the Municipal Government to implement flat pricing and distributed rice at more than ten locations. The small people who eat grain received significant benefits. The harvest of small grains this year was mediocre. After the new wheat entered the market, the price of flour and wheat failed to fall significantly and was subject to manipulation by speculators. After repeated investigations of the accounts, the price gradually declined from July. The price statistics for rice and wheat flour from January to August of the 19th year are listed below.

International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea

The Ministry of Communications Orders Shipping Associations to Provide Opinions

The local shipping association recently received an order from the Ministry of Communications, stating that the British government previously sent a note to us regarding the International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea, asking whether we are willing to join all or part of it. The National Government ordered the Ministry of the Navy and this Ministry to draft opinions and submit them for approval. This Ministry believes that this Convention is very important as it relates to international navigation, and it is appropriate to order the association to submit its opinions before jointly consulting with the Ministry of the Navy to decide whether or not to join, and then submit a reply to the National Government.

Tang Zuan Zhi was publicly elected as the head of the corps and has held the position for many years. Mr. Tang has worked hard and made significant contributions. He previously expressed his intention to resign, but due to the reorganization period and the undetermined funding, he reluctantly continued to serve. Now that the reorganization has been completed and Tang has been appointed as the head of the corps, the funding is being issued monthly by the Reorganization Committee. It is heard that Mr. Tang has recently focused on industry and that the flour mill he planned has opened. It is difficult for him to manage the position of head of the defense corps, and he submitted his resignation to Mayor Zhang of the Shanghai Municipal Government and the members of the Reorganization Committee yesterday.

A Laughing Matter in Free Talk by Hai Ke

A: How do you think this cigarette tastes? If you smoke a thousand of them and send the cartons to the cigarette company, you can get a free travel suitcase.

B: Forget it. If you ask me to smoke half a kilogram of cigarettes in one go, I won't need a suitcase. Just send me a coffin.

Mother (in a tram): Child, stand up quickly and give this seat to the old man. Can't you see he's struggling to hang on to the strap?

Child: Mother, Father likes straps the most. Don't you see he often grabs me with a strap at home? Now he's hanging on a strap, which is exactly what he likes.

Housewife (instructing her dull servant): Ah Wang, go to the butcher shop at the entrance of the lane and ask the fat boss if he has any pig's trotters.

Dull Servant: Yes, Madam. I'll go and see right away. (Returns empty-handed after a while.)

Housewife: How was it? Did you see if he had any pig's trotters?

Dull Servant: Madam, I looked carefully at the fat boss's feet. I saw that he was wearing leather boots and couldn't see any pig's trotters. So I didn't dare ask him.

Wife: Darling, what do you think of this new cloak?

Husband: I think it looks like half a month's salary.

Thoughts on the Xiao Case by Zhao Ding Ming

Ms. Xiao Xin An accepted a position at the Pei De School for Overseas Chinese in Ambon Island, Makassar, in the South Seas. The insults she suffered from the second mate of the Dutch Java Line, the various experiences, and the shared indignation of the Dutch Overseas Chinese and the people of the country have been fully disclosed in this newspaper. We must regard Ms. Xiao's enthusiasm for overseas Chinese education as an exceptional case of a lone woman sailing overseas. The melancholy mood she experienced on the ship cannot be appreciated by travelers who have not personally experienced it. But if we put ourselves in her shoes, we can imagine the kind of terror and anxiety she felt and arouse sympathy. Below are my personal thoughts on the Xiao case.

I seem to have seen Ms. Xiao's face one day at the Oriental Bookstore when Mr. Huang Jing Wan was looking at a large batch of photos attached to the passports of female teachers going to the South Seas. However, because Mr. Huang, who is enthusiastic about social work, was talking and walking in a hurry, I only vaguely compared them. Ms. Xiao's appearance seemed to be more heroic than the other women. But observing their uniformly simple attire and the excited attitude of each, one cannot help but admire their spirit of sacrificing themselves for overseas Chinese education and wish them well. However, less than a month after they set sail on August 14, the newspapers reported that two or three female teachers going to the South Seas were prevented from landing and sent back on the original ship. People with backbone cannot help but feel indignant. On September 26 and 28, various newspapers repeatedly published various reports about the Xiao case. I think that everyone with the blood of the Yellow Emperor race would feel the same excitement about the insults Ms. Xiao suffered. Ms. Xiao, disregarding the heavy damage to her heart and her personal reputation, resolutely revealed everything in detail. At the same time, various associations and schools sent telegrams of support and urged the National Government to seriously negotiate with the Netherlands. I think that any rational country should uphold justice and that the Xiao case should not be difficult to resolve satisfactorily. However, I saw that Ms. Xiao's letter to a friend contained such negative language as "What is the joy of being alive? Life is not worth cherishing. Only my old mother makes me worry about how to reassure her. I am living a few more days only for this." I sincerely hope that Ms. Xiao will not only not be pessimistic in the future, but also not need to be pessimistic. She should promote this great spirit and further express her instinct to serve society. This minor flaw cannot hide her supreme qualities.

Furthermore, I hope that all young men and women of the entire Chinese nation will become enlightened and unite to stand on the front line under the banner of the Blue Sky with a White Sun and move forward. Otherwise, all kinds of humiliation will come one after another.

Small Record of Watching the Tide by Shou Qiu Qing

The sound of the Qiantang River tide is heard at home and abroad. The time of the osmanthus fragrance is especially a great sight. Recorded in history books and spread by word of mouth, those who have not seen it are eager to see it, and those who have seen it are never tired of watching it. The shape of the tide is not uniform, some are large, some are small, some are complete, some are missing, all are like overlapping snow, or like rolling mountains. Watching the tide on a moonlit night is especially interesting. The Qiantang River tide, which is well known, has this majestic and wonderful appearance, which cannot be matched by other places. It is said that the autumn tide this year is extremely large, the largest in more than ten years. When friends meet, they often use this as a topic of conversation. However, since I have been in Hangzhou, I have watched the tide many times. The highest is no more than four or five feet, and the smallest is irrelevant. Although it is the most powerful tide, it has not reached the realm of rushing. I sigh that I am unlucky, so I hesitate. Yesterday, after dinner, my interest in traveling suddenly moved. I went to Jianggan with my second son, Yingwei. It was still early. I sat on the floating boat at the first pier and heard people talk about Jiangshang's affairs, which was quite funny. But Yingwei could no longer bear it, so he went ashore to drink tea at the Guanhai Tower and looked out over the railing. The river was vast, but it was a pity that the building was high and the distance was far, and the tide might not be able to be seen closely. Suddenly, I heard people say that the tide in Xixing was higher and larger than in Jianggan. The highest day was as high as the abdomen of the bus station. The general people waiting for the ferry by the river were almost completely wet. I suddenly realized that there were more ladies crossing the river today than in the past. This is probably the reason. The Xixing River is only ten miles away from the Sanlang Temple. It can be reached in a moment. I took Yingwei on the ferry to the south bank. When I arrived at the shore, the viewers were already crowded like ants. At the end of the pontoon bridge, a large piece had been washed away by the tide. There was still water accumulated on the edge of the embankment. The waves must have been huge. I walked around the station, and the red flag at the ferry had already been raised. The whistle did not sound. I knew the tide was coming. Fearing being affected by the waves, I chose a high place that did not block the view and stood waiting. At this time, the people's voices suddenly rose, and the crowd shouted that the tide was coming. All eyes were focused on the heart of the river. Looking into the distance between the sky and the water, there was a wisp of white thread, appearing and disappearing in the mist. It was getting bigger and bigger, and getting closer and closer, like a rolled-up scroll, like a snowy practice. There was a faint thunder in the air, from small to small, from small to moving. At this time, the atmosphere of heaven and earth and the shape of the characters were unconsciously solemn. In a blink of an eye, the tide was like thousands of troops and horses rolling in, welcoming them. The snow waves were emptying, crossing the river for ten miles, the wind was rising and the clouds were surging, the heart was shocked and the eyes were dizzy. The earth was shocked by it, and the rivers and rivers were twisted. The shore was several feet high, and the waves were still grabbing people. The water was coming from the sky, rushing and leaping, the water was screaming and the thunder was roaring. Alas, how magnificent. This tide is truly a great view of the world. It is also the first original vision of my life. I am privately happy that I seized the opportunity and gained a broad vision. The most wonderful thing is that the tide reaches the edge of the bridge and becomes a cliff of several feet, rushing and flying, forming a strange sight. Those who stand on the edge of the embankment are caught off guard, look at each other and lose color. Those who sit on the railings of the bridge are wet with clothes and shoes, and are in a state of embarrassment. When the frightened souls have just settled down, they can't help but laugh at each other. Bold women taste the same taste, their faces are red, and they are also interesting stories in the sound of the tide. When the tide recedes, the water rises, as high as the embankment. The sound is rumbling, still with a lingering power. Standing

Silk Merchants Request Relief Yesterday's News 105

Request to Issue 10 Million Yuan in Public Bonds: Shanghai silk factory owners report that the silk market is extremely sluggish, factories' capital has been almost entirely depleted, many are unable to continue operations, and the number of closures is increasing daily. If urgent relief measures are not taken, silk factories fear complete bankruptcy. The Silk Factory Association held a special emergency meeting of all factory owners and resolved to petition the government to issue 5 million yuan in silk industry bonds to rescue the silk factory industry in Shanghai. Chairman Shen Huachen and other committee members visited Zhang Shouyong, the Vice Minister of Finance, to personally explain the depressed state of the silk market. Vice Minister Zhang agreed to consider the matter further after receiving a detailed plan for issuing silk industry bonds and repayment methods. It is now learned that silk factory owners in Wuxi,

Hangzhou, Jiaxing, Huzhou, and other cities all believe that this year's silk industry slump is unprecedented and fraught with danger. Silk factories in all regions are facing the same difficult conditions and should jointly appeal to the government along with Shanghai merchants. Representatives are now being sent to Shanghai to discuss cooperation with the Silk Market Relief Committee organized by the Shanghai Silk Factory Association and decide on a joint petition to the National Government's Ministry of Finance and Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting the issuance of 10 million yuan in silk industry bonds to provide widespread support. It is reported that representatives from silk factory owners in Shanghai, Wuxi, Hangzhou, Jiaxing, Huzhou, and other places have formed the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Factory Industry Relief Committee in Shanghai to jointly plan action.

In fact, in this difficult living environment, we workers are already groaning and suffering beyond measure, and the evil Japanese capitalists are stirring up trouble, frequently adding oppression, reducing the original wages of the factory's workers by forty percent while increasing the workload by more than half. Such actions treat us laborers worse than cattle and horses. Their disregard for our nation is evident. The silk weaving workers of the Shanghai Silk Factory have been on strike for half a month. On the one hand, they are making empty promises, and on the other hand, they are using reactionary forces to force workers to return to the factory. In fact, their strategy is simply to make the workers yield. Our union, standing with the workers, cannot bear to stand idly by, like Qin Yue Ren ignoring the thin and weak, letting fellow laborers be oppressed and leaving a disgrace on the Shanghai labor movement. Therefore, we loudly appeal, hoping that all sectors will show sympathy, so that the hundreds of pitiful workers in the silk weaving department of the Shanghai Silk Factory can achieve final victory. Rather be a shattered jade than a whole tile, we vow to fight against the Japanese imperialist capitalists. Let all sectors be aware of this. In addition to jointly petitioning the superior authorities, we hereby declare, Shanghai Inland River Steamboat Union, Cleaning Industry First Special District Labor Union, Yutong Silk Weaving Union, Minsheng Yarn Factory Union, Huazhuang Binding Special District Labor Union, Bookstore Industry Union, Hongzhang Textile Union, China Industrial Silk Weaving Factory Union.

Concession Police Arrest a Large Group of Bandits 110

Informant Reports Kidnapping

Police Unable to Confirm Yet

Fountain Pen Pistol Is Terrifying

A Puff of Smoke Causes Unconsciousness

Planned Kidnapping: Su Yinggen, a Chinese detective in the Concession Police, received a report on the 4th of this month from an informant, stating that a group of bandits intended to kidnap a resident surnamed in Taoyuan Lane on Huisan Road. Detective Su reported this to the police chief, who, along with Chinese Detective Chief Zhang Zhiqing, Su Changsheng, Patrol Detective Yang Xichen, Li Lianchuan, Liu Xuecheng, Chen Lianjing, Shi Baoying, and other Chinese and Western detectives on duty, disguised themselves and scattered around Taoyuan Lane to lie in ambush. At around 5:00 PM, a car with the number 2085 drove up and circled the entrance of Taoyuan Lane (there are seven entrances to this lane) four times for about twenty minutes before stopping at the intersection of Huisan Road and Zhoushan Road.

Waiting for the Leader Here: Three people jumped out of the car and stood by the road, whispering to each other. Detective Li Lianchuan happened to be standing next to them and heard them say that there were many patrols nearby today, so it would not be easy to succeed. They should come back tomorrow. They also asked Detective Li who he was. Li replied that he was a comrade waiting for the leader here (the organization of these bandits was quite complex, so they did not recognize their own comrades).

Three Bandits Arrested Shortly After: Soon after, the three were about to get back into the car and leave when they were captured by the detectives lying in ambush. The car was also seized and taken to the police station. Under questioning, the three bandits identified themselves as Qian Xingsheng, He Wenqing, and Zhou Rucai. Detective Chief Su searched the car and found three pistols and twenty bullets near the engine.

Leader's Wife and Children Apprehended: He also revealed that their leader was Wu Junling, from Anhui, who lived at No. 313 Kunming Road. The pistols and car belonged to Wu. Chinese and Western detectives went to No. 313 Kunming Road to arrest Wu, but Wu had already fled. Only his wife, Jin, his son, Peigong (also known as Peiyun), and accomplices Jin Lilin (also known as Lielin), Wu Shikui, Wang A Jin, and Wang Tong were arrested.

Fountain Pen Pistol: Many Communist Party commission documents appointing Wu as some kind of commander were found in the house, as well as a fountain pen-style pistol. The pistol was similar to a fountain pen, but slightly larger. It had a mechanism on top and contained a bullet. However, the bullet could not kill a person. It was filled with poison. Simply triggering the mechanism would shoot out the poison, which would turn into a puff of smoke. Anyone who inhaled it would become unconscious and would not wake up for half an hour. Wu's possession of this gun was intended to make the kidnap victim lose consciousness after being kidnapped so that they could not call for help along the way. His thoroughness shows that he is experienced in this matter. The detectives then took them all to the police station.

More Bandits Apprehended Later: The police also ordered detectives to wait in the house. Later, they successively arrested Zhu Shiping, Su Baorong, Yu Ruili, Zhou Junchao (Zhou is the principal of a school in Huzhou). The detectives also continued to arrest Xie Desheng, Ma Wencai, Xie Zheng, and three others at No. 996 Taopeng Road and brought them back to the police station.

Fresh Ink on the Sign: Wu Peigong confessed that his father had a Xinxin Paper Factory at the end of Taopeng Road. Chinese and Western detectives went to the paper factory to arrest him. When they arrived at the factory, they saw that the sign had been changed to Minghua, but the ink on the sign was not yet dry, indicating that it had not been changed for long. They then took the manager of the paper factory, Song Guangfu, and the sign back to the police station and detained them separately.

Leader Has Repeatedly Committed Major Crimes: Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the Special District Court. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, stated the case and said that the leader of this gang of bandits, Wu Junling, had repeatedly committed major crimes in the past. The former Provisional Court and your court had issued arrest warrants. There were as many as four arrest warrants. The police had not yet determined whether the defendants' actions were kidnapping or robbery, so they were temporarily prosecuting them under Article 161 of the Criminal Law for the crime of forming a gang of bandits. They would revise the charges after the investigation was clear.

Rescheduled for Special Hearing: Today, the case could not proceed based on the situation. A request was made to reschedule it for a special hearing in the afternoon. The defendant Wu Jin and Wu Peigong hired Fan Gang as their lawyer. Judge Feng Shide briefly questioned the defendants and ordered them to be returned to custody and rescheduled for a special hearing.

Another Principal Offender in the Embezzlement of Large Sums of Money Arrested 111

Chen Jianji and His Wife

Chen Used the Alias Tang Baoshan

Visited the East Asia Hotel in Broad Daylight

Recognized Only After Seeing the Photo

Banknotes Found in the Soles of Shoes

Chen Jianji and Bai Rishuan, the accounting officer and deputy accounting officer of the German-owned Lide Foreign Firm in Sha Ji, Guangdong, recently colluded to embezzle 33,000 yuan of the firm's money and fled to Shanghai. The firm's principal found out and telegraphed the German Consulate in Shanghai, which forwarded the matter to the General Police Station for investigation. On the night of the 3rd of this month, Chinese detectives Pang Ruiqing, Feng Zhiming, Wang Chengying, Feng Shuofu, and Western Detective Chief Baideng from the General Inspection Office arrested Bai Rishuan and He Rong, a tea server at Lide Foreign Firm, in Room 320 of the East Asia Hotel on Nanjing Road. Chen had escaped. After Bai and He were escorted to the Special Court for preliminary hearing, the court ordered that Bai and He be handed over to Public Security Bureau detectives for transfer to the Guangzhou Court for trial. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now it is learned that the police, after Bai and others were arrested, still sent Chinese and Western detectives to wait in the room. At 5:30 PM on the 4th (Saturday), Chen Jianji, who had fled, under the alias Tang Baoshan, and his wife, Chen Tang, under the alias Tang Huang, visited Room 320 of the East Asia Hotel to inquire about Bai. The Chinese and Western detectives took out photos, and after checking them, they knew that he was Chen Jianji. They arrested Chen and his wife and took them to the police station. Under questioning, Chen still denied being Chen Jianji and claimed to be Tang Baoshan. The police chief then telephoned the Municipal Public Security Bureau and brought Bai and He back to the police station. Chen was mixed among the crowd of criminals and Bai was asked to identify him. Bai immediately pointed out Chen, and Chen bowed his head and said nothing. A 2,000 yuan note from the Deda Money Shop was found on Chen. Chen Tang was also searched by a female investigator, but nothing was found. Chen was ordered to be detained and Tang was sent to the women's detention center of the Special Court. Upon further searching, more than 3,000 yuan in Hong Kong HSBC banknotes, each worth 500 yuan, were found in the soles of her shoes. However, some of the banknotes had been torn by Tang. Yesterday morning, Chen and his wife were escorted to the First Criminal Court of the Special Court. Judge Zhou Hanting took the bench and interrogated them. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, presented the case and requested that the two defendants be transferred to the Public Security Bureau so that they could be transferred to the Guangzhou Court for interrogation along with Bai and the others. However, a 2,000 yuan note found on the defendant could be taken away by the German Consulate upon presentation of a receipt, because the police's case was based on the report of the German Consulate and the German Consulate had the qualification to represent the plaintiff. Wang Shenqing, an investigator from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, then submitted a document requesting transfer. When questioned, the defendant Chen Jianji confessed, "This matter was done by me alone and has nothing to do with Bai. I left my job on the 25th of last month and obtained 2,100 yuan in cash and a 25,000 yuan check from the company at that time. On the 4th of this month, I arrived in Shanghai with my wife and stayed at Room 3 of the Hongkou Hotel on North Sichuan Road. I went to the East Asia Hotel yesterday to visit Bai Rishuan after he was arrested. Bai's reason for coming to Shanghai was to open a gambling table, so the 2,000 yuan note confiscated by the police was remitted from Xiamen to Shanghai and could be exchanged for money. The money was entrusted by a friend for me to receive, so that it could be used as capital to join Bai's gambling table." When questioned, Chen Tang confessed, "I know nothing about this matter. This time, I came to Shanghai with my husband to travel. The more than 3,000 yuan in banknotes that were confiscated were also entrusted to me by my husband to carry on his behalf." After Judge Zhou checked the confessions, he ordered that the two defendants be handed over to the Public Security Bureau to be transferred to the Guangzhou Court for interrogation along with Bai and the others. The banknotes and notes would be temporarily kept in the police station for verification. The two defendants were then taken down by detectives. As soon as they left the courthouse door, Chen Tang suddenly said, "I carried a total of 10,000 yuan this time. The money was obtained by selling a house in Xiamen when we set off. Now that more than 3,000 yuan has been confiscated, there is still more than 6,000 yuan, but I don't know where it was lost." The Chinese and Western detectives were surprised to hear this, thinking that there might be other circumstances involved, so they took her to the police station for investigation.
